<li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques0"><strong>Question 1. What Is Oracle?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Oracle is a company. Oracle is also a database server, which manages data in a very structured way. It allows users to store and retrieve related data in a multiuser environment so that many users can concurrently access the same data. All this is accomplished while delivering high performance. A database server also prevents unauthorized access and provides efficient solutions for failure recovery.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1"><strong>Question 2. What Is An Oracle Database?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>An Oracle database is a collection of data treated as a big unit in the database server.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques2"><strong>Question 3. What Is An Oracle Instance?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Every running Oracle database is associated with an Oracle instance. When a database is started on a database server (regardless of the type of computer), Oracle allocates a memory area called the System Global Area (SGA) and starts one or more Oracle processes. This combination of the SGA and the Oracle processes is called an Oracle instance. The memory and processes of an instance manage the associated database's data efficiently and serve the one or multiple users of the database.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques3"><strong>Question 4. What Is Oracle Table? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>A table is the basic unit of data storage in an Oracle database. The tables of a database hold all of the user accessible data. Table data is stored in rows and columns.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques4"><strong>Question 5. What Is An Oracle View? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>A view is a virtual table. Every view has a query attached to it. (The query is a SELECT statement that identifies the columns and rows of the table(s) the view uses.)</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques5"><strong>Question 6. What Is An Oracle Sequence? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>A sequence generates a serial list of unique numbers for numerical columns of a database's tables.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques6"><strong>Question 7. What Is An Oracle Index? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>An index is an optional structure associated with a table to have direct access to rows, which can be created to increase the performance of data retrieval. Index can be created on one or more columns of a table.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques7"><strong>Question 8. What Is An Oracle Data File?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>An Oracle data file is a big unit of physical storage in the OS file system. One or many Oracle data files are organized together to provide physical storage to a single Oracle tablespace.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques8"><strong>Question 9. What Are The Components Of Physical Database Structure Of Oracle Database?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Oracle database is comprised of three types of files. One or more datafiles, two are more redo log files, and one or more control files.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques9"><strong>Question 10. What Are The Components Of Logical Database Structure Of Oracle Database? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>There are tablespaces and database's schema objects.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques10"><strong>Question 11. What Is A Tablespace?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>A database is divided into Logical Storage Unit called tablespaces. A tablespace is used to grouped related logical structures together.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques11"><strong>Question 12. What Is System Tablespace And When Is It Created? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Every Oracle database contains a tablespace named SYSTEM, which is automatically created when the database is created. The SYSTEM tablespace always contains the data dictionary tables for the entire database.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques12"><strong>Question 13. Explain The Relationship Among Database, Tablespace And Data File ?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Each databases logically divided into one or more tablespaces one or more data files are explicitly created for each tablespace.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques13"><strong>Question 14. What Is Schema? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>A schema is collection of database objects of a user.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques14"><strong>Question 15. What Are Schema Objects? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Schema objects are the logical structures that directly refer to the database's data. Schema objects include tables, views, sequences, synonyms, indexes, clusters, database triggers, procedures, functions packages and database links.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques15"><strong>Question 16. Can Objects Of The Same Schema Reside In Different Tablespaces? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Yes.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques16"><strong>Question 17. Can A Tablespace Hold Objects From Different Schemes? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Yes.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques17"><strong>Question 18. What Is Partial Backup ? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>A Partial Backup is any operating system backup short of a full backup, taken while the database is open or shut down.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques18"><strong>Question 19. What Is Mirrored On-line Redo Log ?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>A mirrored on-line redo log consists of copies of on-line redo log files physically located on separate disks, changes made to one member of the group are made to all members.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques19"><strong>Question 20. What Is Full Backup ? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>A full backup is an operating system backup of all data files, on-line redo log files and control file that constitute ORACLE database and the parameter.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques20"><strong>Question 21. Can A View Based On Another View ? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Yes.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques21"><strong>Question 22. Can A Tablespace Hold Objects From Different Schemes ? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Yes.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques22"><strong>Question 23. Can Objects Of The Same Schema Reside In Different Tablespace ? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Yes.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques23"><strong>Question 24. What Is The Use Of Control File ? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>When an instance of an ORACLE database is started, its control file is used to identify the database and redo log files that must be opened for database operation to proceed. It is also used in database recovery.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques24"><strong>Question 25. Do View Contain Data ? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Views do not contain or store data.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques25"><strong>Question 26. What Are The Referential Actions Supported By Foreign Key Integrity Constraint ? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p><strong>UPDATE and DELETE Restrict</strong> - A referential integrity rule that disallows the update or deletion of referenced data.<br/>
<strong>DELETE Cascade</strong> - When a referenced row is deleted all associated dependent rows are deleted.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques26"><strong>Question 27. What Are The Type Of Synonyms? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>There are two types of Synonyms</p>
<ul>
<li>Private </li>
<li>Public.</li>
</ul></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques27"><strong>Question 28. What Is A Redo Log ? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>The set of Redo Log files YSDATE,UID,USER or USERENV SQL functions, or the pseudo columns LEVEL or ROWNUM.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques28"><strong>Question 29. What Is An Index Segment ? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Each Index has an Index segment that stores all of its data.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques29"><strong>Question 30. Explain The Relationship Among Database, Tablespace And Data File? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Each databases logically divided into one or more tablespaces one or more data files are explicitly created for each tablespace.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques30"><strong>Question 31. What Are The Different Type Of Segments ? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>The different type of Segments are:</p>
<ul>
<li>Data Segment,</li>
<li>Index Segment,</li>
<li>Rollback Segment and</li>
<li>Temporary Segment.</li>
</ul></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques31"><strong>Question 32. What Are Clusters ? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Clusters are groups of one or more tables physically stores together to share common columns and are often used together.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques32"><strong>Question 33. What Is An Integrity Constrains ? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>An integrity constraint is a declarative way to define a business rule for a column of a table.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques33"><strong>Question 34. What Is An Index ? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>An Index is an optional structure associated with a table to have direct access to rows, which can be created to increase the performance of data retrieval. Index can be created on one or more columns of a table.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques34"><strong>Question 35. What Is An Extent ? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>An Extent is a specific number of contiguous data blocks, obtained in a single allocation, and used to store a specific type of information.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques35"><strong>Question 36. What Is A View ? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>A view is a virtual table. Every view has a Query attached to it. (The Query is a SELECT statement that identifies the columns and rows of the table(s) the view uses.)</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques36"><strong>Question 37. What Is Table ? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>A table is the basic unit of data storage in an ORACLE database. The tables of a database hold all of the user accessible data. Table data is stored in rows and columns.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques37"><strong>Question 38. Can A View Based On Another View?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Yes.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques38"><strong>Question 39. What Are The Advantages Of Views? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><ul>
<li>Provide an additional level of table security, by restricting access to a predetermined set of rows and columns of a table.</li>
<li>Hide data complexity.</li>
<li>Simplify commands for the user.</li>
<li>Present the data in a different perspective from that of the base table.</li>
<li>Store complex queries.</li>
</ul></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques39"><strong>Question 40. What Is A Synonym? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>A synonym is an alias for a table, view, sequence or program unit.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques40"><strong>Question 41. What Are The Types Of Synonyms? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>There are two types of synonyms private and public.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques41"><strong>Question 42. What Is A Private Synonym? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Only its owner can access a private synonym.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques42"><strong>Question 43. What Is A Public Synonym? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Any database user can access a public synonym.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques43"><strong>Question 44. What Are Synonyms Used For? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><ul>
<li>Mask the real name and owner of an object.</li>
<li>Provide public access to an object.</li>
<li>Provide location transparency for tables, views or program units of a remote database.</li>
<li>Simplify the SQL statements for database users.</li>
</ul></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques44"><strong>Question 45. How Are The Index Updates? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Indexes are automatically maintained and used by Oracle. Changes to table data are automatically incorporated into all relevant indexes.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques45"><strong>Question 46. What Is Rollback Segment ? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>A Database contains one or more Rollback Segments to temporarily store "undo" information.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques46"><strong>Question 47. What Are The Characteristics Of Data Files ? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>A data file can be associated with only one database. Once created a data file can't change size. One or more data files form a logical unit of database storage called a tablespace.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques47"><strong>Question 48. How To Define Data Block Size ? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>A data block size is specified for each ORACLE database when the database is created. A database users and allocated free database space in ORACLE data blocks. Block size is specified in INIT.ORA file and can’t be changed latter.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques48"><strong>Question 49. What Does A Control File Contain ? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>A Control file records the physical structure of the database. It contains the following information. </p>
<ul>
<li>Database Name</li>
<li>Names and locations of a database's files and redolog files.</li>
<li>Time stamp of database creation.</li>
</ul></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques49"><strong>Question 50. What Is Difference Between Unique Constraint And Primary Key Constraint ?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>A column defined as UNIQUE can contain Nulls while a column defined as PRIMARY KEY can't contain Nulls.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques50"><strong>Question 51. What Is Index Cluster ? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>A Cluster with an index on the Cluster Key.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques51"><strong>Question 52. When Does A Transaction End ? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>When it is committed or Rollbacked.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques52"><strong>Question 53. What Is The Effect Of Setting The Value "all_rows" For Optimizer_goal Parameter Of The Alter Session Command ? What Are The Factors That Affect Optimizer In Choosing An Optimization Approach ? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>The OPTIMIZER_MODE initialization parameter Statistics in the Data Dictionary the OPTIMIZER_GOAL parameter of the ALTER SESSION command hints in the statement.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques53"><strong>Question 54. What Is The Effect Of Setting The Value "choose" For Optimizer_goal, Parameter Of The Alter Session Command ? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>The Optimizer chooses Cost_based approach and optimizes with the goal of best throughput if statistics for atleast one of the tables accessed by the SQL statement exist in the data dictionary. Otherwise the OPTIMIZER chooses RULE_based approach.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques54"><strong>Question 55. How Does One Create A New Database? (for Dba) </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>One can create and modify Oracle databases using the Oracle "dbca" (Database Configuration Assistant) utility. The dbca utility is located in the $ORACLE_HOME/bin directory. The Oracle Universal Installer (oui) normally starts it after installing the database server software.</p>
<p>One can also create databases manually using scripts. This option, however, is falling out of fashion, as it is quite involved and error prone. Look at this example for creating and Oracle 9i database:</p>
<pre>
CONNECT SYS AS SYSDBA<br/>ALTER SYSTEM SET DB_CREATE_FILE_DEST='/u01/oradata/';<br/>ALTER SYSTEM SET DB_CREATE_ONLINE_LOG_DEST_1='/u02/oradata/';<br/>ALTER SYSTEM SET DB_CREATE_ONLINE_LOG_DEST_2='/u03/oradata/';<br/>CREATE DATABASE;</pre></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques55"><strong>Question 56. What Database Block Size Should I Use? (for Dba) </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Oracle recommends that your database block size match, or be multiples of your operating system block size. One can use smaller block sizes, but the performance cost is significant. Your choice should depend on the type of application you are running. If you have many small transactions as with OLTP, use a smaller block size. With fewer but larger transactions, as with a DSS application, use a larger block size. If you are using a volume manager, consider your "operating system block size" to be 8K. This is because volume manager products use 8K blocks (and this is not configurable).</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques56"><strong>Question 57. What Are The Different Approaches Used By Optimizer In Choosing An Execution Plan ? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>The different approaches used by Optimizer in choosing an execution plan are:</p>
<ul>
<li>Rule-based</li>
<li>Cost-based.</li>
</ul></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques57"><strong>Question 58. What Does Rollback Do ? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>ROLLBACK retracts any of the changes resulting from the SQL statements in the transaction.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques58"><strong>Question 59. What Is Cost-based Approach To Optimization ? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Considering available access paths and determining the most efficient execution plan based on statistics in the data dictionary for the tables accessed by the statement and their associated clusters and indexes.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques59"><strong>Question 60. What Does Commit Do ? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>COMMIT makes permanent the changes resulting from all SQL statements in the transaction. The changes made by the SQL statements of a transaction become visible to other user sessions transactions that start only after transaction is committed.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques60"><strong>Question 61. How Are Extents Allocated To A Segment? (for Dba) </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Oracle8 and above rounds off extents to a multiple of 5 blocks when more than 5 blocks are requested. If one requests 16K or 2 blocks (assuming a 8K block size), Oracle doesn't round it up to 5 blocks, but it allocates 2 blocks or 16K as requested. If one asks for 8 blocks, Oracle will round it up to 10 blocks. </p>
<p>Space allocation also depends upon the size of contiguous free space available. If one asks for 8 blocks and Oracle finds a contiguous free space that is exactly 8 blocks, it would give it you. If it were 9 blocks, Oracle would also give it to you. Clearly Oracle doesn't always round extents to a multiple of 5 blocks. </p>
<p>The exception to this rule is locally managed tablespaces. If a tablespace is created with local extent management and the extent size is 64K, then Oracle allocates 64K or 8 blocks assuming 8K-block size. Oracle doesn't round it up to the multiple of 5 when a tablespace is locally managed.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques61"><strong>Question 62. Can One Rename A Database User (schema)? (for Dba) </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>No, this is listed as Enhancement Request 158508. Workaround:</p>
<ul>
<li>Do a user-level export of user A</li>
<li>create new user B</li>
<li>Import system/manager fromuser=A touser=B</li>
<li>Drop user A</li>
</ul></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques62"><strong>Question 63. Define Transaction ?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>A Transaction is a logical unit of work that comprises one or more SQL statements executed by a single user.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques63"><strong>Question 64. What Is Read-only Transaction ? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>A Read-Only transaction ensures that the results of each query executed in the transaction are consistant with respect to the same point in time.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques64"><strong>Question 65. What Is A Deadlock ? Explain </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Two processes wating to update the rows of a table which are locked by the other process then deadlock arises. In a database environment this will often happen because of not issuing proper row lock commands. Poor design of front-end application may cause this situation and the performance of server will reduce drastically.</p>
<p>These locks will be released automatically when a commit/rollback operation performed or any one of this processes being killed externally.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques65"><strong>Question 66. What Is A Schema ? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>The set of objects owned by user account is called the schema.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques66"><strong>Question 67. What Is A Cluster Key ? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>The related columns of the tables are called the cluster key. The cluster key is indexed using a cluster index and its value is stored only once for multiple tables in the cluster.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques67"><strong>Question 68. What Is Parallel Server ? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Multiple instances accessing the same database (Only In Multi-CPU environments)</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques68"><strong>Question 69. What Is Clusters ? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Group of tables physically stored together because they share common columns and are often used together is called Cluster.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques69"><strong>Question 70. What Is An Index ? How It Is Implemented In Oracle Database ? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>An index is a database structure used by the server to have direct access of a row in a table. An index is automatically created when a unique of primary key constraint clause is specified in create table comman (Ver 7.0).</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques70"><strong>Question 71. What Is A Database Instance ? Explain </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>A database instance (Server) is a set of memory structure and background processes that access a set of database files.</p>
<p>The process can be shared by all users. The memory structure that are used to store most queried data from database. This helps up to improve database performance by decreasing the amount of I/O performed against data file.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques71"><strong>Question 72. What Is The Use Of Analyze Command ? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>To perform one of these function on an index, table, or cluster:</p>
<ul>
<li>To collect statistics about object used by the optimizer and store them in the data dictionary.</li>
<li>To delete statistics about the object used by object from the data dictionary.</li>
<li>To validate the structure of the object.</li>
<li>To identify migrated and chained rows of the table or cluster.</li>
</ul></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques72"><strong>Question 73. What Is Default Tablespace ? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>The Tablespace to contain schema objects created without specifying a tablespace name.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques73"><strong>Question 74. What Are The System Resources That Can Be Controlled Through Profile ? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>The number of concurrent sessions the user can establish the CPU processing time available to the user's session the CPU processing time available to a single call to ORACLE made by a SQL statement the amount of logical I/O available to the user's session the amout of logical I/O available to a single call to ORACLE made by a SQL statement the allowed amount of idle time for the user's session the allowed amount of connect time for the user's session.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques74"><strong>Question 75. What Is Tablespace Quota ? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>The collective amount of disk space available to the objects in a schema on a particular tablespace.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques75"><strong>Question 76. What Are The Different Levels Of Auditing ? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>The different Levels of Auditing are:</p>
<ul>
<li>Statement Auditing,</li>
<li>Privilege Auditing and</li>
<li>Object Auditing.</li>
</ul></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques76"><strong>Question 77. What Is Statement Auditing ? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Statement auditing is the auditing of the powerful system privileges without regard to specifically named objects.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques77"><strong>Question 78. What Are The Database Administrators Utilities Available ? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><ul>
<li><strong>SQL * DBA</strong> - This allows DBA to monitor and control an ORACLE database.</li>
<li><strong>SQL * Loader</strong> - It loads data from standard operating system files (Flat files) into ORACLE database tables.</li>
<li><strong>Export (EXP) and Import (imp)</strong> utilities allow you to move existing data in ORACLE format to and from ORACLE database.</li>
</ul></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques78"><strong>Question 79. How Can You Enable Automatic Archiving ? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><ul>
<li>Shut the database</li>
<li>Backup the database</li>
<li>Modify/Include LOG_ARCHIVE_START_TRUE in init.ora file.</li>
<li>Start up the database.</li>
</ul></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques79"><strong>Question 80. What Are Roles? How Can We Implement Roles ? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Roles are the easiest way to grant and manage common privileges needed by different groups of database users. Creating roles and assigning provides to roles. Assign each role to group of users. This will simplify the job of assigning privileges to individual users.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques80"><strong>Question 81. What Are Roles ? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Roles are named groups of related privileges that are granted to users or other roles.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques81"><strong>Question 82. What Are The Use Of Roles ? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>The use of Roles are:</p>
<ul>
<li><em><strong>REDUCED GRANTING OF PRIVILEGES</strong></em> - Rather than explicitly granting the same set of privileges to many users a database administrator can grant the privileges for a group of related users granted to a role and then grant only the role to each member of the group.</li>
<li><em><strong>DYNAMIC PRIVILEGE MANAGEMENT </strong></em>- When the privileges of a group must change, only the privileges of the role need to be modified. The security domains of all users granted the group's role automatically reflect the changes made to the role.</li>
<li><em><strong>SELECTIVE AVAILABILITY OF PRIVILEGES</strong></em> - The roles granted to a user can be selectively enable (available for use) or disabled (not available for use). This allows specific control of a user's privileges in any given situation.</li>
<li><em><strong>APPLICATION AWARENESS</strong></em> - A database application can be designed to automatically enable and disable selective roles when a user attempts to use the application.</li>
</ul></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques82"><strong>Question 83. What Is Privilege Auditing ? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Privilege auditing is the auditing of the use of powerful system privileges without regard to specifically named objects.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques83"><strong>Question 84. What Is Object Auditing ? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Object auditing is the auditing of accesses to specific schema objects without regard to user.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques84"><strong>Question 85. What Is Auditing ? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Monitoring of user access to aid in the investigation of database use.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques85"><strong>Question 86. Where Are My Tempfiles, I Don't See Them In V$datafile Or Dba_data_file? (for Dba )</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Tempfiles, unlike normal datafiles, are not listed in v$datafile or dba_data_files. Instead query v$tempfile or dba_temp_files:</p>
<ul>
<li>SELECT * FROM v$tempfile;</li>
<li>SELECT * FROM dba_temp_files;</li>
</ul></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques86"><strong>Question 87. How Do I Find Used/free Space In A Temporary Tablespace? (for Dba )</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Unlike normal tablespaces, true temporary tablespace information is not listed in DBA_FREE_SPACE. Instead use the V$TEMP_SPACE_HEADER view:</p>
<ul>
<li>SELECT tablespace_name, SUM (bytes used), SUM (bytes free)</li>
<li>FROM V$temp_space_header</li>
<li>GROUP BY tablespace_name;</li>
</ul></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques87"><strong>Question 88. What Is A Profile ? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Each database user is assigned a Profile that specifies limitations on various system resources available to the user.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques88"><strong>Question 89. How Will You Enforce Security Using Stored Procedures? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Don't grant user access directly to tables within the application. Instead grant the ability to access the procedures that access the tables. When procedure executed it will execute the privilege of procedures owner. Users cannot access tables except via the procedure.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques89"><strong>Question 90. How Does One Get The View Definition Of Fixed Views/tables? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Query v$fixed_view_definition. Example: SELECT * FROM v$fixed_view_definition WHERE view_name= 'V$SESSION';</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques90"><strong>Question 91. What Are The Dictionary Tables Used To Monitor A Database Spaces ? </strong></a></p>

<ul>

<li>DBA_SEGMENTS</li>
<li>DBA_DATA_FILES.</li>
</ul></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques91"><strong>Question 92. How Can We Specify The Archived Log File Name Format And Destination? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>By setting the following values in init.ora file. LOG_ARCHIVE_FORMAT = arch %S/s/T/tarc (%S - Log sequence number and is zero left paded, %s - Log sequence number not padded. %T - Thread number lef-zero-paded and %t - Thread number not padded). The file name created is arch 0001 are if %S is used. LOG_ARCHIVE_DEST = path.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques92"><strong>Question 93. What Is User Account In Oracle Database? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>An user account is not a physical structure in Database but it is having important relationship to the objects in the database and will be having certain privileges.</p></p>

</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques94"><strong>Question 95. What Dynamic Data Replication? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Updating or Inserting records in remote database through database triggers. It may fail if remote database is having any problem.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques95"><strong>Question 96. What Is Two-phase Commit ? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Two-phase commit is mechanism that guarantees a distributed transaction either commits on all involved nodes or rolls back on all involved nodes to maintain data consistency across the global distributed database. It has two phase, a Prepare Phase and a Commit Phase.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques96"><strong>Question 97. How Can You Enforce Referential Integrity In Snapshots ? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Time the references to occur when master tables are not in use. Peform the reference the manually immediately locking the master tables. We can join tables in snopshots by creating a complex snapshots that will based on the master tables.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques97"><strong>Question 98. What Is A Sql * Net? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>SQL *NET is ORACLE's mechanism for interfacing with the communication protocols used by the networks that facilitate distributed processing and distributed databases. It is used in Clint-Server and Server-Server communications.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques98"><strong>Question 99. What Is A Snapshot ? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Snapshots are read-only copies of a master table located on a remote node which is periodically refreshed to reflect changes made to the master table.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques99"><strong>Question 100. What Is The Mechanism Provided By Oracle For Table Replication ? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Snapshots and SNAPSHOT LOGs.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques100"><strong>Question 101. What Is Snapshots? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Snapshot is an object used to dynamically replicate data between distribute database at specified time intervals. In ver 7.0 they are read only.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques101"><strong>Question 102. What Are The Various Type Of Snapshots? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>The various type of snapshots are:</p>
<ul>
<li>Simple </li>
<li>Complex.</li>
</ul></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques102"><strong>Question 103. Describe Two Phases Of Two-phase Commit ? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p><em><strong>Prepare phase</strong></em> - The global coordinator (initiating node) ask a participants to prepare (to promise to commit or rollback the transaction, even if there is a failure).<br/>
<em><strong> Commit  Phase</strong></em> - If all participants respond to the coordinator that they are prepared, the coordinator asks all nodes to commit the transaction, if all participants cannot prepare, the coordinator asks all nodes to roll back the transaction.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques103"><strong>Question 104. What Is Snapshot Log ? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>It is a table that maintains a record of modifications to the master table in a snapshot. It is stored in the same database as master table and is only available for simple snapshots. It should be created before creating snapshots.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques104"><strong>Question 105. What Are The Benefits Of Distributed Options In Databases? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><ul>
<li>Database on other servers can be updated and those transactions can be grouped together with others in a logical unit.</li>
<li>Database uses a two phase commit.</li>
</ul></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques105"><strong>Question 106. What Are The Options Available To Refresh Snapshots ? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p><strong>COMPLETE</strong> - Tables are completely regenerated using the snapshots query and the master tables every time the snapshot referenced.<br/>
<strong>FAST</strong> - If simple snapshot used then a snapshot log can be used to send the changes to the snapshot tables.<br/>
<strong>FORCE</strong> - Default value. If possible it performs a FAST refresh; Otherwise it will perform a complete refresh.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques106"><strong>Question 107. What Is A Snapshot Log ?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>A snapshot log is a table in the master database that is associated with the master table. ORACLE uses a snapshot log to track the rows that have been updated in the master table. Snapshot logs are used in updating the snapshots based on the master table.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques107"><strong>Question 108. What Is Distributed Database ? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>A distributed database is a network of databases managed by multiple database servers that appears to a user as single logical database. The data of all databases in the distributed database can be simultaneously accessed and modified.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques108"><strong>Question 109. How Can We Reduce The Network Traffic? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><ul>
<li>Replication of data in distributed environment.</li>
<li>Using snapshots to replicate data.</li>
<li>Using remote procedure calls.</li>
</ul></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques109"><strong>Question 110. Differentiate Simple And Complex, Snapshots ? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><ul>
<li>A simple snapshot is based on a query that does not contains GROUP BY clauses, CONNECT BY clauses, JOINs, sub-query or snashot of operations.</li>
<li>A complex snapshots contain atleast any one of the above.</li>
</ul></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques110"><strong>Question 111. What Are The Built-ins Used For Sending Parameters To Forms? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>You can pass parameter values to a form when an application executes the call_form, New_form, Open_form or Run_product.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques111"><strong>Question 112. Can You Have More Than One Content Canvas View Attached With A Window? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Yes. Each window you create must have atleast one content canvas view assigned to it. You can also create a window that has manipulated content canvas view. At run time only one of the content canvas views assign to a window is displayed at a time.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques112"><strong>Question 113. Is The After Report Trigger Fired If The Report Execution Fails? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Yes.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques113"><strong>Question 114. Does A Before Form Trigger Fire When The Parameter Form Is Suppressed? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Yes.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques114"><strong>Question 115. What Is Sga?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>The System Global Area in an Oracle database is the area in memory to facilitate the transfer of information between users. It holds the most recently requested structural information between users. It holds the most recently requested structural information about the database. The structure is database buffers, dictionary cache, redo log buffer and shared pool area.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques115"><strong>Question 116. What Is A Shared Pool? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>The data dictionary cache is stored in an area in SGA called the shared pool. This will allow sharing of parsed SQL statements among concurrent users.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques116"><strong>Question 117. What Is Mean By Program Global Area (pga)? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>It is area in memory that is used by a single Oracle user process.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques117"><strong>Question 118. What Is A Data Segment? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Data segment are the physical areas within a database block in which the data associated with tables and clusters are stored.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques118"><strong>Question 119. What Are The Factors Causing The Reparsing Of Sql Statements In Sga? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><ul>
<li>Due to insufficient shared pool size.</li>
<li>Monitor the ratio of the reloads takes place while executing SQL statements. If the ratio is greater than 1 then increase the SHARED_POOL_SIZE.</li>
</ul></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques119"><strong>Question 120. What Are Clusters? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Clusters are groups of one or more tables physically stores together to share common columns and are often used together.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques120"><strong>Question 121. What Is Cluster Key? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>The related columns of the tables in a cluster are called the cluster key.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques121"><strong>Question 122. Do A View Contain Data? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Views do not contain or store data.</p></p>

<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>When-image-activated fires when the operators double clicks on an image item when-image-pressed fires when an operator clicks or double clicks on an image item.</p></p>

<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques130"><strong>Question 131. What Is Difference Between Open_form And Call_form? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>when one form invokes another form by executing open_form the first form remains displayed, and operators can navigate between the forms as desired. when one form invokes another form by executing call_form, the called form is modal with respect to the calling form. That is, any windows that belong to the calling form are disabled, and operators cannot navigate to them until they first exit the called form.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques131"><strong>Question 132. What Is New_form Built-in? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>When one form invokes another form by executing new_form oracle form exits the first form and releases its memory before loading the new form calling new form completely replace the first with the second. If there are changes pending in the first form, the operator will be prompted to save them before the new form is loaded.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques132"><strong>Question 133. What Is The "lov Of Validation" Property Of An Item? What Is The Use Of It? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>When LOV for Validation is set to True, Oracle Forms compares the current value of the text item to the values in the first column displayed in the LOV. Whenever the validation event occurs. If the value in the text item matches one of the values in the first column of the LOV, validation succeeds, the LOV is not displayed, and processing continues normally. If the value in the text item does not match one of the values in the first column of the LOV, Oracle Forms displays the LOV and uses the text item value as the search criteria to automatically reduce the list.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">

<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques149"><strong>Question 150. What Are The Two Phases Of Block Coordination? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>There are two phases of block coordination:</p>
<p><strong>The clear phase:</strong>During, the clear phase, Oracle Forms navigates internally to the detail block and flushes the obsolete detail records.</p>
<p><strong>The population phase</strong>.  During the population phase, Oracle Forms issues a SELECT statement to repopulate the detail block with detail records associated with the new master record. These operations are accomplished through the execution of triggers.</p></p>

<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques172"><strong>Question 173. What Are Difference Between Post Database Commit And Post-form Commit? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p><strong>Post-form commit</strong> fires once during the post and commit transactions process, after the database commit occurs. The post-form-commit trigger fires after inserts, updates and deletes have been posted to the database but before the transactions have been finalized in the issuing the command.<br/>
<strong>post-database-commit </strong>trigger fires after oracle forms issues the commit to finalized transactions.</p></p>

<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques179"><strong>Question 180. What Is An Administrative (privileged) User? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Oracle DBAs and operators typically use administrative accounts to manage the database and database instance. An administrative account is a user that is granted SYSOPER or SYSDBA privileges. SYSDBA and SYSOPER allow access to a database instance even if it is not running. Control of these privileges is managed outside of the database via password files and special operating system groups. This password file is created with the orapwd utility.</p></p>

<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques182"><strong>Question 183. How Does One Create A Password File? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>The Oracle Password File ($ORACLE_HOME/dbs/orapw or orapwSID) stores passwords for users with administrative privileges. One needs to create a password files before remote administrators (like OEM) will be allowed to connect.</p>
<p>Follow this procedure to create a new password file:</p>
<ul>
<li>Log in as the Oracle software owner</li>
<li>Runcommand: orapwd file=$ORACLE_HOME/dbs/orapw$ORACLE_SID password=mypasswd</li>
<li>Shutdown the database (SQLPLUS&gt; SHUTDOWN IMMEDIATE)</li>
<li>Edit the INIT.ORA file and ensure REMOTE_LOGIN_PASSWORDFILE=exclusive is set.</li>
<li>Startup the database (SQLPLUS&gt; STARTUP)</li>
</ul></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">

</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques187"><strong>Question 188. Why Are Ops$ Accounts A Security Risk In A Client/server Environment? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>If you allow people to log in with OPS$ accounts from Windows Workstations, you cannot be sure who they really are. With terminals, you can rely on operating system passwords, with Windows, you cannot.</p>
<p>If you set REMOTE_OS_AUTHENT=TRUE in your init.ora file, Oracle assumes that the remote OS has authenticated the user. If REMOTE_OS_AUTHENT is set to FALSE (recommended), remote users will be unable to connect without a password. IDENTIFIED EXTERNALLY will only be in effect from the local host. Also, if you are using "OPS$" as your prefix, you will be able to log on locally with or without a password, regardless of whether you have identified your ID with a password or defined it to be IDENTIFIED EXTERNALLY.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">

</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques198"><strong>Question 199. What Is The Advantage Of The Library?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Libraries provide a convenient means of storing client-side program units and sharing them among multiple applications. Once you create a library, you can attach it to any other form, menu, or library modules. When you can call library program units from triggers menu items commands and user named routine, you write in the modules to which you have attach the library. When a library attaches another library, program units in the first library can reference program units in the attached library. Library support dynamic loading-that is library program units are loaded into an application only when needed. This can significantly reduce the run-time memory requirements of applications.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques199"><strong>Question 200. What Is Lexical Reference? How Can It Be Created? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Lexical reference is place_holder for text that can be embedded in a sql statements. A lexical reference can be created using &amp; before the column or parameter name.</p></p>

<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques218"><strong>Question 219. What Is When-database-record Trigger? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Fires when oracle forms first marks a record as an insert or an update. The trigger fires as soon as oracle forms determines through validation that the record should be processed by the next post or commit as an insert or update. c generally occurs only when the operators modifies the first item in the record, and after the operator attempts to navigate out of the item.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques219"><strong>Question 220. What Is A Difference Between Pre-select And Pre-query? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Fires during the execute query and count query processing after oracle forms constructs the select statement to be issued, but before the statement is actually issued. The pre-query trigger fires just before oracle forms issues the select statement to the database after the operator as define the example records by entering the query criteria in enter query mode.Pre-query trigger fires before pre-select trigger.</p></p>

<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques225"><strong>Question 226. Why And When Should One Tune? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>One of the biggest responsibilities of a DBA is to ensure that the Oracle database is tuned properly. The Oracle RDBMS is highly tunable and allows the database to be monitored and adjusted to increase its performance. One should do performance tuning for the following reasons: </p>
<p>The speed of computing might be wasting valuable human time (users waiting for response); Enable your system to keep-up with the speed business is conducted; and Optimize hardware usage to save money (companies are spending millions on hardware). Although this FAQ is not overly concerned with hardware issues, one needs to remember than you cannot tune a Buick into a Ferrari.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">

<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques241"><strong>Question 242. Does One Need To Drop/ Truncate Objects Before Importing?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Before one import rows into already populated tables, one needs to truncate or drop these tables to get rid of the old data. If not, the new data will be appended to the existing tables. One must always DROP existing Sequences before re-importing. If the sequences are not dropped, they will generate numbers inconsistent with the rest of the database. </p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">

</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques243"><strong>Question 244. Can One Import/export Between Different Versions Of Oracle?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Different versions of the import utility is upwards compatible. This means that one can take an export file created from an old export version, and import it using a later version of the import utility. This is quite an effective way of upgrading a database from one release of Oracle to the next.</p>
<p>Oracle also ships some previous catexpX.sql scripts that can be executed as user SYS enabling older imp/exp versions to work (for backwards compatibility). For example, one can run $ORACLE_HOME /rdbms /admin/catexp7.sql on an Oracle 8 database to allow the Oracle 7.3 exp/imp utilities to run against an Oracle 8 database.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">

</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques251"><strong>Question 252. What Is The Difference Between Ole Server &amp; Ole Container? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p><strong>Ole server</strong> application creates ole Objects that are embedded or linked in ole Containers ex. Ole servers are ms_word &amp; ms_excel.<br/>
<strong>OLE containers</strong> provide a place to store, display and manipulate objects that are created by ole server applications. Ex. oracle forms is an example of an ole Container.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques252"><strong>Question 253. What Is An Object Group? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>An object group is a container for a group of objects; you define an object group when you want to package related objects, so that you copy or reference them in other modules.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques253"><strong>Question 254. What Is An Lov? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>An LOV is a scrollable popup window that provides the operator with either a single or multi column selection list.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques254"><strong>Question 255. At What Point Of Report Execution Is The Before Report Trigger Fired? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>After the query is executed but before the report is executed and the records are displayed.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques255"><strong>Question 256. What Are The Built -ins Used For Modifying A Groups Structure? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><ul>
<li>ADD-GROUP_COLUMN (function)</li>
<li>ADD_GROUP_ROW (procedure)</li>
<li>DELETE_GROUP_ROW(procedure)</li>
</ul></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques256"><strong>Question 257. What Is An User Exit Used For? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>A way in which to pass control (and possibly arguments ) form Oracle report to another Oracle products of 3 GL and then return control ( and ) back to Oracle reports.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques257"><strong>Question 258. What Is The User-named Editor? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>A user named editor has the same text editing functionality as the default editor, but, because it is a named object, you can specify editor attributes such as windows display size, position, and title.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques258"><strong>Question 259. What Is A Static Record Group? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>A static record group is not associated with a query, rather, you define its structure and row values at design time, and they remain fixed at runtime.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques259"><strong>Question 260. What Is A Record Group? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>A record group is an internal Oracle Forms that structure that has a column/row framework similar to a database table. However, unlike database tables, record groups are separate objects that belong to the form module which they are defined.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques260"><strong>Question 261. My Database Is Down And I Cannot Restore. What Now? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Recovery without any backup is normally not supported, however, Oracle Consulting can sometimes extract data from an offline database using a utility called DUL (Disk UnLoad). This utility reads data in the data files and unloads it into SQL*Loader or export dump files. DUL does not care about rollback segments, corrupted blocks, etc, and can thus not guarantee that the data is not logically corrupt. It is intended as an absolute last resort and will most likely cost your company a lot of money!!!</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques261"><strong>Question 262. I've Lost My Redolog Files, How Can I Get My Db Back? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>The following INIT.ORA parameter may be required if your current redo logs are corrupted or blown away. Caution is advised when enabling this parameter as you might end-up losing your entire database. Please contact Oracle Support before using it. <br/>
_allow_resetlogs_corruption = true</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques262"><strong>Question 263. What Is A Property Clause? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>A property clause is a named object that contains a list of properties and their settings. Once you create a property clause you can base other object on it. An object based on a property can inherit the setting of any property in the clause that makes sense for that object.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques263"><strong>Question 264. What Is A Physical Page &amp; What Is A Logical Page ? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>A physical page is a size of a page. That is output by the printer. The logical page is the size of one page of the actual report as seen in the Previewer.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques264"><strong>Question 265. What Are The Differences Between Ebu And Rman?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Enterprise Backup Utility (EBU) is a functionally rich, high performance interface for backing up Oracle7 databases. It is sometimes referred to as OEBU for Oracle Enterprise Backup Utility. The Oracle Recovery Manager (RMAN) utility that ships with Oracle8 and above is similar to Oracle7's EBU utility. However, there is no direct upgrade path from EBU to RMAN.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques265"><strong>Question 266. How Does One Create A Rman Recovery Catalog? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Start by creating a database schema (usually called rman). Assign an appropriate tablespace to it and grant it the recovery_catalog_owner role. Look at this example: </p>
<pre>
sqlplus sys<br/>SQL&gt;create user rman identified by rman;<br/>SQL&gt; alter user rman default tablespace tools temporary tablespace temp;<br/>SQL&gt; alter user rman quota unlimited on tools;<br/>SQL&gt; grant connect, resource, recovery_catalog_owner to rman;<br/>SQL&gt; exit;</pre>
<p>Next, log in to rman and create the catalog schema. Prior to Oracle 8i this was  done by running the catrman.sql script. rman catalog rman/rman</p>
<pre>
RMAN&gt;create catalog tablespace tools;<br/>RMAN&gt; exit;</pre>
<p>You can now continue by registering your databases in the catalog. Look at this  example: <br/>
rman catalog rman/rman target backdba/backdba</p>
<pre>
RMAN&gt; register database;</pre></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques266"><strong>Question 267. How Can A Group In A Cross Products Be Visually Distinguished From A Group That Does Not Form A Cross Product? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>A group that forms part of a cross product will have a thicker border.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques267"><strong>Question 268. What Is The Frame &amp; Repeating Frame? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>A frame is a holder for a group of fields. A repeating frame is used to display a set of records when the no. of records that are to displayed is not known before.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques268"><strong>Question 269. What Is A Combo Box? </strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>A combo box style list item combines the features found in list and text item. Unlike the pop list or the text list style list items, the combo box style list item will both display fixed values and accept one operator entered value.</p></p>
