<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques893"><strong>Question 894. What Are Autonomous Transactions? Give A Scenario Where You Have Used Autonomous Transaction In Your Reports?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>An autonomous transaction is an independent transaction started by another transaction, the main transaction. Autonomous transactions let you suspend the main transaction, do SQL operations, commit or roll back those operations, then resume the main transaction. Once started, an autonomous transaction is fully independent. It shares no locks, resources, or commit-dependencies with the main transaction. So, you can log events, increment retry counters, and so on, even if the main transaction rolls back.</p>
<p>More important, autonomous transactions help you build modular, reusable software components. For example, stored procedures can start and finish autonomous transactions on their own. A calling application need not know about a procedure's autonomous operations, and the procedure need not know about the application's transaction context. That makes autonomous transactions less error-prone than regular transactions and easier to use.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques894"><strong>Question 895. What Are Snapshots? What Are Materialized Views &amp; Where Do We Use Them? What Is A Materialized View Log?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Snapshots are read-only copies of a master table located on a remote node which is periodically refreshed to reflect changes made to the master table. Snapshots are mirror or replicas of tables.</p>
<p>Views are built using the columns from one or more tables. The Single Table View can be updated but the view with multi table cannot be updated.</p>
<p>A View can be updated/deleted/inserted if it has only one base table if the view is based on columns from one or more tables then insert, update and delete is not possible.</p>
<p><em><strong>Materialized view</strong></em> : A pre-computed table comprising aggregated or joined data from fact and possibly dimension tables. Also known as a summary or aggregate table.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques895"><strong>Question 896. When Do We Analyze The Tables? How Do We Do It?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>The ANALYZE statement allows you to validate and compute statistics for an index, table, or cluster. These statistics are used by the cost-based optimizer when it calculates the most efficient plan for retrieval. In addition to its role in statement optimization, ANALYZE also helps in validating object structures and in managing space in your system. You can choose the following operations: </p>
<p>COMPUTER, ESTIMATE, and DELETE. Early version of Oracle7 produced unpredicatable results when the ESTIMATE operation was used. It is best to compute your statistics.</p>
<p>EX:</p>
<pre>
select OWNER,
sum(decode(nvl(NUM_ROWS,9999), 9999,0,1))analyzed,
sum(decode(nvl(NUM_ROWS,9999), 9999,1,0))not_analyzed,
count(TABLE_NAME) total
from dba_tables
where OWNER not in ('SYS', 'SYSTEM')
group by OWNER</pre>
<p> </p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">

<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques902"><strong>Question 903. What Is A Mapping, Session, Worklet, Workflow, Mapplet?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>A mapping represents dataflow from sources to targets.</p>
<p>A mapplet creates or configures a set of transformations.</p>
<p>A workflow is a set of instruction sthat tell the Informatica server how to execute the tasks.</p>
<p>A worklet is an object that represents a set of tasks.</p>
<p>A session is a set of instructions that describe how and when to move data from sources to targets.</p></p>

<p>If you require dynamic cache i.e where your data will change dynamically then you can go for connceted lookup.If your data is static where your data won't change when the session loads you can go for unconnected lookups.</p></p>

<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques922"><strong>Question 923. What Are Snapshots? What Are Materialized Views &amp; Where Do We Use Them? What Is A Materialized View?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Materialized view is a view in wich data is also stored in some temp table.i.e if we will go with the View concept in DB in that we only store query and once we call View it extract data from DB. <p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques925"><strong>Question 926. At What Stage Is The Subledger Data Posted To Gl?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Basically after entering the transactions, report will be taken to verify the transactions. In case, if approval is needed, it is approved after verifying the transactions. Once you are sure that the transactions are correct, the same can be posted to GL. Once it is posted, most of the informations for the posted transaction can not be modified in the subledger. In case of any wrong entry, you need to follow the reversal procedure.</p>
<p>Practically, the verification of transactions are done only during the initial stages after implementation. Once the system becomes stable, it is not followed strictly.</p></p>

<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques928"><strong>Question 929. What Is Meant By Adi?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>ADI is used to interface spreadsheet uploads with Oracle applications data. ADI allows users take advantage of many of the data-entry shortcuts of a spreadsheet, such as copying and pasting cells, dragging and dropping ranges of cells and using formulas to calculate journal line amounts. ADI validates the data entered against the accounts, security rules and reference information that are defined in the General Ledger (GL).</p></p>

<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques946"><strong>Question 947. What Are Different Types Of Journal Entries?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>There are 4 types of journal entries.</p>
<ol>
<li>Basic Journal Entry - Used for most of the accounting transactions.</li>
<li>Reversing JE - Created by reversing the existing journal entry.</li>
<li>Recurring JE - Defined once and then generated for subsequent accounting period.</li>
<li>Mass Allocation - Created to allocate the revenues and assets to a group of resources(cost centers, depts, divisions,etc) from a single Journal.</li>
</ol></p>

<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques951"><strong>Question 952. What Is The Difference Between Cross-validation Rules And Security-rules?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p><em><strong>Cross Validation Rule </strong></em>: Rules that define valid combinations of segment values a user can enter in an account. Cross-validation rules restrict users from entering invalid combinations of account segment values.</p>
<p><em><strong>Security Rule </strong></em>: It determines the accounting transaction user can view at differenty levels of hierarchy, such as at Site Level --&gt;Application Level --&gt; Responsibility Level --&gt; User level.</p></p>

<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques957"><strong>Question 958. What Are Summary Accounts And Rollup Groups?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Summary Account is an account whose balance represents the sum of other account balances. You can use summary accounts for faster reporting and inquiry as well as in formulas and allocations.</p>
<p>Rollup group is a collection of parent segment values for a given segment. You use rollup groups to define summary accounts based on parents in the group. You can use letters as well as numbers to name your rollup groups.</p></p>

<p>Both can be executed any number of times. Only difference is that stored procedures / functions are stored in database in complied format while the application procedures/functions are not in precomplied format and at run time has to be compiled.</p></p>

<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques962"><strong>Question 963. How We Can Create A Table In Pl/sql Block. Insert Records Into It? Is It Possible By Some Procedure Or Function? Please Give Example?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><pre>
CREATE OR REPLACE PROCEDURE ddl_create_proc
(p_table_name IN VARCHAR2)
AS
l_stmt VARCHAR2(200);
BEGIN
DBMS_OUTPUT.put_line('STARTING ');
l_stmt := 'create table '|| p_table_name ||
 ' as (select * from emp )';
execute IMMEDIATE l_stmt;
DBMS_OUTPUT.put_line('end ');
EXCEPTION
WHEN OTHERS THEN
DBMS_OUTPUT.put_line
('exception '||SQLERRM || 'message'||sqlcode);
END;</pre></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques963"><strong>Question 964. How To Avoid Using Cursors? What To Use Instead Of Cursor And In What Cases To Do So?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Just use subquery in for clause</p>
<p>ex:</p>
<pre>
For emprec in (select * from emp)
loop
dbms_output.put_line(emprec.empno);
end loop;
</pre>
<p>no exit statement needed implicit open,fetch,close occurs.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques964"><strong>Question 965. State The Difference Between Implict And Explict Cursors?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Implicit Cursor are declared and used by the oracle internally. whereas the explicit cursors are declared and used by the user. more over implicitly cursors are no need to declare oracle creates and process and closes autometically. the explicit cursor should be declared and closed by the user. </p>
<p>Implicit cursors are used for single row query whereas explicit cursor is used for multiple row query.</p></p>

<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques968"><strong>Question 969. What Are The Components Of A Pl/sql Block?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>A set of related declarations and procedural statements is called block.</p>
<p><em><strong>DECLARE </strong></em>-- declaration section </p>
<p><em><strong>BEGIN </strong></em>-- executable statements -- main section </p>
<p><em><strong>EXCEPTION</strong></em> -- handling possible exceptions -- occuring in the main section END;</p></p>

<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques970"><strong>Question 971. What Are % Type And % Rowtype? What Are The Advantages Of Using These Over Datatypes?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>% TYPE provides the data type of a variable or a database column to that variable.</p>
<p>% ROWTYPE provides the record type that represents a entire row of a table or view or columns selected in the cursor.</p>
<p><em><strong>The advantages are </strong></em>: I. Need not know about variable's data type ii. If the database definition of a column in a table changes, the data type of a variable changes accordingly.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">

<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques972"><strong>Question 973. What Is A Database Trigger? Name Some Usages Of Database Trigger?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Database trigger is stored PL/SQL program unit associated with a specific database table. Usages are Audit data modifications, Log events transparently, Enforce complex business rules Derive column values automatically, Implement complex security authorizations. Maintain replicate tables.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques973"><strong>Question 974. What Is Raise_application_error?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Raise_application_error is a procedure of package DBMS_STANDARD which allows to issue an user_defined error messages from stored sub-program or database trigger.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques974"><strong>Question 975. What Are The Return Values Of Functions Sqlcode And Sqlerrm?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>SQLCODE returns the latest code of the error that has occurred.</p>
<p>SQLERRM returns the relevant error message of the SQLCODE.</p></p>

<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques977"><strong>Question 978. Explain The Two Type Of Cursors?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>There are two types of cursors, Implicit Cursor and Explicit Cursor.</p>
<p>PL/SQL uses Implicit Cursors for queries. User defined cursors are called Explicit Cursors. They can be declared and used.</p></p>

<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques982"><strong>Question 983. What Is Multi Org Architecture?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>The Multiorg Architecture is meant to allow multiple companies or subsidiaries to store their records within a single database. The multiple Organization architecture allows this by partitioning data through views in the APPS schema. Multiorg also allows you to maintain multiple sets of books. </p>
<p>Implementation of multiorg generally includes defining more than one Business Group.</p></p>

<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1004"><strong>Question 1005. How Do You Implement One-to-one, One-to-many And Many-to-many Relationships While Designing Tables?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>One-to-One relationship can be implemented as a single table and rarely as two tables with primary and foreign key relationships.</p>
<p>One-to-Many relationships are implemented by splitting the data into two tables with primary key and foreign key relationships.</p>
<p>Many-to-Many relationships are implemented using a junction table with the keys from both the tables forming the composite primary key of the junction table.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1005"><strong>Question 1006. If A View On A Single Base Table Is Manipulated Will The Changes Be Reflected On The Base Table?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>If changes are made to the tables and these tables are the base tables of a view, then the changes will be reference on the view.</p></p>

<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>A View can be updated/deleted/inserted if it has only one base table if the view is based on columns from one or more tables then insert, update and delete is not possible.</p></p>

<li>To hide complexity of a query.</li>
<li>To hide complexity of calculations.</li>
</ul></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1008"><strong>Question 1009. What Is Cycle/no Cycle In A Sequence?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>CYCLE specifies that the sequence continue to generate values after reaching either maximum or minimum value. After pan-ascending sequence reaches its maximum value, it generates its minimum value. After a descending sequence reaches its minimum, it generates its maximum.</p>
<p>NO CYCLE specifies that the sequence cannot generate more values after reaching its maximum or minimum value.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1009"><strong>Question 1010. How To Access The Current Value And Next Value From A Sequence? Is It Possible To Access The Current Value In A Session Before Accessing Next Value?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Sequence name CURRVAL, sequence name NEXTVAL. It is not possible. Only if you access next value in the session, current value can be accessed.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1010"><strong>Question 1011. What Is A Database Link?</strong></a></p>

</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">

<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1014"><strong>Question 1015. What Are The Pre-requisites To Modify Datatype Of A Column And To Add A Column With Not Null Constraint?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><ul>
<li>To modify the datatype of a column the column must be empty.</li>
<li>To add a column with NOT NULL constrain, the table must be empty.</li>
</ul></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1015"><strong>Question 1016. How Many Long Columns Are Allowed In A Table? Is It Possible To Use Long Columns In Where Clause Or Order By?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Only one LONG column is allowed. It is not possible to use LONG column in WHERE or ORDER BY clause.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1016"><strong>Question 1017. What Is Difference Between Char And Varchar2? What Is The Maximum Size Allowed For Each Type?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>CHAR pads blank spaces to the maximum length.</p>
<p>VARCHAR2 does not pad blank spaces.</p>
<p>For CHAR the maximum length is 255 and 2000 for VARCHAR2.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1017"><strong>Question 1018. What Are The Data Types Allowed In A Table?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>CHAR, VARCHAR2, NUMBER, DATE, RAW, LONG and LONG RAW.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1018"><strong>Question 1019. What Is On Delete Cascade?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>When ON DELETE CASCADE is specified Oracle maintains referential integrity by automatically removing dependent foreign key values if a referenced primary or unique key value is removed.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1019"><strong>Question 1020. What Is The Usage Of Savepoints?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>SAVEPOINTS are used to subdivide a transaction into smaller parts. It enables rolling back part of a transaction. Maximum of five save points are allowed.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1020"><strong>Question 1021. What Is Referential Integrity Constraint?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Maintaining data integrity through a set of rules that restrict the values of one or more columns of the tables based on the values of primary key or unique key of the referenced table.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1021"><strong>Question 1022. What Is An Integrity Constraint?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Integrity constraint is a rule that restricts values to a column in a table.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1022"><strong>Question 1023. What Is The Fastest Way Of Accessing A Row In A Table?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Using ROWID, CONSTRAINTS.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1023"><strong>Question 1024. What Is Rowid?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>ROWID is a pseudo column attached to each row of a table. It is 18 characters long, blockno, rownumber are the components of ROWID.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1024"><strong>Question 1025. Explain Union, Minus, Union All And Intersect?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p><em><strong>INTERSECT</strong></em> - returns all distinct rows selected by both queries.</p>
<p><em><strong>MINUS</strong></em> - returns all distinct rows selected by the first query but not by the second.</p>
<p><em><strong>UNION </strong></em>- returns all distinct rows selected by either query.</p>
<p><em><strong>UNION ALL </strong></em>- returns all rows selected by either query, including all duplicates.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1025"><strong>Question 1026. What Is Correlated Sub-query?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Correlated sub-query is a sub-query, which has reference to the main query.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1026"><strong>Question 1027. What Is The Sub-query?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Sub-query is a query whose return values are used in filtering conditions of the main query.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1027"><strong>Question 1028. What Is A Join? Explain The Different Types Of Joins?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Join is a query, which retrieves related columns or rows from multiple tables.</p>
<p><em><strong>Self Join</strong></em> - Joining the table with itself.</p>
<p><em><strong>Equi Join </strong></em>- Joining two tables by equating two common columns.</p>
<p><em><strong>Non-Equi Join </strong></em>- Joining two tables by equating two common columns.</p>
<p><em><strong>Outer Join</strong></em> - Joining two tables in such a way that query can also retrieve rows that do not have corresponding join value in the other table.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1028"><strong>Question 1029. What Is Difference Between Truncate &amp; Delete?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>TRUNCATE commits after deleting entire table i.e., cannot be rolled back. Database triggers do not fire on TRUNCATE.</p>
<p>DELETE allows the filtered deletion. Deleted records can be rolled back or committed. Database triggers fire on DELETE.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1029"><strong>Question 1030. What Is A Transaction?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Transaction is logical unit between two commits and commit and rollback.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1030"><strong>Question 1031. What Are The Types Of Sql Statement?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p><em><strong>Data Definition Language: </strong></em>CREATE, ALTER, DROP, TRUNCATE, REVOKE, NO AUDIT &amp; COMMIT.</p>
<p><em><strong>Data Manipulation Language:</strong></em> INSERT, UPDATE, DELETE, LOCK TABLE, EXPLAIN PLAN &amp; SELECT.</p>
<p><em><strong>Transactional Control:</strong></em> COMMIT &amp; ROLLBACK.</p>
<p><em><strong>Session Control:</strong></em> ALTERSESSION &amp; SET ROLE.</p>
<p><em><strong>System Control: </strong></em>ALTER SYSTEM.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1031"><strong>Question 1032. List The Factors That Can Affect The Accuracy Of The Estimations?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><ul>
<li>The space used transaction entries and deleted records, does not become free immediately after completion due to delayed cleanout.</li>
<li>Trailing nulls and length bytes are not stored.</li>
<li>Inserts of, updates to and deletes of rows as well as columns larger than a single data block, can cause fragmentation a chained row pieces.</li>
</ul></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1032"><strong>Question 1033. What Are Disadvantages Of Having Raw Devices?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>We should depend on export / import utility for backup / recovery (fully reliable) The tar command cannot be used for physical file backup, instead we can use dd command, which is less flexible and has limited recoveries.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1033"><strong>Question 1034. When Will Be A Segment Released?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><ul>
<li>When Segment is dropped.</li>
<li>When Shrink (RBS only).</li>
<li>When truncated (TRUNCATE used with drop storage option).</li>
</ul></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1034"><strong>Question 1035. What Is Hit Ratio?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>It is a measure of well the data cache buffer is handling requests for data.</p>
<p>Hit Ratio = (Logical Reads - Physical Reads - Hits Misses)/ Logical Reads.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1035"><strong>Question 1036. What Is A Rollback Segment Entry?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>It is the set of before image data blocks that contain rows that are modified by a transaction. Each rollback segment entry must be completed within one rollback segment.</p>
<p>A single rollback segment can have multiple rollback segment entries.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1036"><strong>Question 1037. What Is Use Of Rollback Segments In Oracle Database?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>They allow the database to maintain read consistency between multiple transactions.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1037"><strong>Question 1038. What Is Advantage Of Having Disk Shadowing / Mirroring?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Shadow set of disks save as a backup in the event of disk failure. In most operating systems if any disk failure occurs it automatically switchover to place of failed disk.</p>
<p>Improved performance because most OS support volume shadowing can direct file I/O request to use the shadow set of files instead of the main set of files. This reduces I/O load on the main set of disks.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1038"><strong>Question 1039. What Is Redo Log File Mirroring? How Can Be Achieved?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Process of having a copy of redo log files is called mirroring.</p>
<p>This can be achieved by creating group of log files together, so that LGWR will automatically writes them to all the members of the current on-line redo log group. If any one group fails then database automatically switch over to next group. It degrades performance.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1039"><strong>Question 1040. How To Implement The Multiple Control Files For An Existing Database?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><ul>
<li>Shutdown the database</li>
<li>Copy one of the existing controlfile to new location</li>
<li>Edit Config ora file by adding new control filename</li>
<li>Restart the database.</li>
</ul></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1040"><strong>Question 1041. What Is A Control File?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Database's overall physical architecture is maintained in a file called control file. It will be used to maintain internal consistency and guide recovery operations. Multiple copies of control files are advisable.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1041"><strong>Question 1042. It Is Possible To Use Raw Devices As Data Files And What Are The Advantages Over File System Files?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Yes.</p>
<p>The advantages over file system files are that I/O will be improved because Oracle is bye-passing the kernel which writing into disk. Disk corruption will be very less.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1042"><strong>Question 1043. How Can We Plan Storage For Very Large Tables?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><ul>
<li>Limit the number of extents in the table.</li>
<li>Separate table from its indexes.</li>
<li>Allocate sufficient temporary storage.</li>
</ul></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1043"><strong>Question 1044. How Will You Monitor The Space Allocation?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>By querying DBA_ SEGMENT table / view.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1044"><strong>Question 1045. Why Query Fails Sometimes?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Rollback segment dynamically extent to handle larger transactions entry loads.</p>
<p>A single transaction may wipeout all available free space in the rollback segment tablespace. This prevents other user using rollback segments.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1045"><strong>Question 1046. How The Space Utilization Takes Place Within Rollback Segments?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>It will try to fit the transaction in a cyclic fashion to all existing extents. Once it found an extent is in use then it forced to acquire a new extent (number of extents is based on the optimal size).</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1046"><strong>Question 1047. How Will You Create Multiple Rollback Segments In A Database?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><ul>
<li>Create a database, which implicitly creates a SYSTEM rollback segment in a SYSTEM tablespace.</li>
<li>Create a second rollback segment name R0 in the SYSTEM tablespace.</li>
<li>Make new rollback segment available (after shutdown, modify init.ora file and start database)</li>
<li>Create other tablespaces (RBS) for rollback segments.</li>
<li>Deactivate rollback segment R0 and activate the newly created rollback segments.</li>
</ul></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1047"><strong>Question 1048. What Is The Functionality Of System Table Space?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>To manage the database level transactions such as modifications of the data dictionary table that record information about the free space usage.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1048"><strong>Question 1049. What Is The Role Of Pctfree Parameter Is Storage Clause?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>This is used to reserve certain amount of space in a block for expansion of rows.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1049"><strong>Question 1050. How Does Space Allocation Table Place Within A Block?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Each block contains entries as follows</p>
<ul>
<li>Fixed block header.</li>
<li>Variable block header.</li>
<li>Row Header, row date (multiple rows may exists).</li>
<li>PCTEREE (% of free space for row updating in future).</li>
</ul></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1050"><strong>Question 1051. What Is The Significance Of Having Storage Clause?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>We can plan the storage for a table as how much initial extents are required, how much can be extended next, how much % should leave free for managing row updating, etc.,</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1051"><strong>Question 1052. Which Parameter In Storage Clause Will Reduce Number Of Rows Per Block?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>PCTFREE parameter Row size also reduces no of rows per block.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1052"><strong>Question 1053. What Is Meant By Free Extent?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>A free extent is a collection of continuous free blocks in tablespace. When a segment is dropped its extents are reallocated and are marked as free.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1053"><strong>Question 1054. How Will You Force Database To Use Particular Rollback Segment?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>SET TRANSACTION USE ROLLBACK SEGMENT rbs_name.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1054"><strong>Question 1055. List The Optional Flexible Architecture (ofa) Of Oracle Database? How Can We Organize The Tablespaces In Oracle Database To Have Maximum Performance?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p><em><strong>SYSTEM </strong></em>- Data dictionary tables.</p>
<p><em><strong>DATA </strong></em>- Standard operational tables.</p>
<p><em><strong>DATA2</strong></em>- Static tables used for standard operations.</p>
<p><em><strong>INDEXES</strong></em> - Indexes for Standard operational tables.</p>
<p><em><strong>INDEXES1</strong></em> - Indexes of static tables used for standard operations.</p>
<p><em><strong>TOOLS</strong></em> - Tools table.</p>
<p><em><strong>TOOLS1</strong></em> - Indexes for tools table.</p>
<p><em><strong>RBS </strong></em>- Standard Operations Rollback Segments.</p>
<p><em><strong>RBS1,RBS2</strong></em> - Additional/Special Rollback segments.</p>
<p><em><strong>TEMP</strong></em> - Temporary purpose tablespace.</p>
<p><em><strong>TEMP_USER</strong></em> - Temporary tablespace for users.</p>
<p><em><strong>USERS </strong></em>- User tablespace.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1055"><strong>Question 1056. How Will You Swap Objects Into A Different Table Space For An Existing Database?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><ul>
<li>Export the user</li>
<li>Perform import using the command imp system/manager file=export.dmp indexfile=newrite.sql. This will create all definitions into newfile.sql.</li>
<li>Drop necessary objects.</li>
<li>Run the script newfile.sql after altering the tablespaces.</li>
<li>Import from the backup for the necessary objects.</li>
</ul></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1056"><strong>Question 1057. What Is Redo Log Buffer?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Changes made to the records are written to the on-line redo log files. So that they can be used in roll forward operations during database recoveries. Before writing them into the redo log files, they will first brought to redo log buffers in SGA and LGWR will write into files frequently. LOG_BUFFER parameter will decide the size.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1057"><strong>Question 1058. What Is Meant By Recursive Hints?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Number of times processes repeatedly query the dictionary table is called recursive hints. It is due to the data dictionary cache is too small. By increasing the SHARED_ POOL_ SIZE parameter we can optimize the size of data dictionary cache.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1058"><strong>Question 1059. What Is Dictionary Cache?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Dictionary cache is information about the database objects stored in a data dictionary table.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1059"><strong>Question 1060. What Is Database Buffers?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Database buffers are cache in the SGA used to hold the data blocks that are read from the data segments in the database such as tables, indexes and clusters DB_ BLOCK_ BUFFERS parameter in INIT. ORA decides the size.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1060"><strong>Question 1061. What Is A Deadlock? Explain?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Two processes waiting to update the rows of a table, which are locked by other processes then deadlock arises.</p>
<p>In a database environment this will often happen because of not issuing the proper row lock commands. Poor design of front-end application may cause this situation and the performance of server will reduce drastically.</p>
<p>These locks will be released automatically when a commit/rollback operation performed or any one of this processes being killed externally.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1061"><strong>Question 1062. What Is A Cluster Key?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>The related columns of the tables are called the cluster key. The cluster key is indexed using a cluster index and its value is stored only once for multiple tables in the cluster.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1062"><strong>Question 1063. What Is An Index? How It Is Implemented In Oracle Database?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>An index is a database structure used by the server to have direct access of a row in a table. An index is automatically created when a unique of primary key constraint clause is specified in create table command.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1063"><strong>Question 1064. What Is A Schema?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>The set of objects owned by user account is called the schema.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1064"><strong>Question 1065. What Is Parallel Server?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Multiple instances accessing the same database (only in multi-CPU environments).</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1065"><strong>Question 1066. What Is A Database Instance? Explain?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>A database instance (Server) is a set of memory structure and background processes that access a set of database files. The processes can be shared by all of the users.</p>
<p>The memory structure that is used to store the most queried data from database. This helps up to improve database performance by decreasing the amount of I/O performed against data file.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1066"><strong>Question 1067. How To Connect Asp Pages To Oracle Servers?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>How To Connect ASP Pages to Oracle Servers? If you are running Windows IIS Web server and serving ASP Web pages, you can get data from Oracle servers into your ASP pages through ODBC drivers. To do this, you need to install the correct Oracle ODBC driver and define a DSN on the IIS Web server.</p>
<p>Then you can use ADODB objects to connect to the Oracle server over the ODBC driver in your ASP pages. The tutorial example below gives you a good example:</p>
<pre>
&lt;%
Set oConn = Server.CreateObject("ADODB.Connection")
oConn.Open "DSN=FYI_DSN;UID=fyi;PWD=retneciyf"
Set oRS = oConn.Execute("SELECT * FROM dev_faq")
Response.write("&lt;p&gt;Data from Oracle server via ODBC:")
Response.write("&lt;pre&gt;")
Do While NOT oRS.EOF
Response.Write(oRS("ID") &amp; vbcrlf)
oRS.MoveNext
Loop
Response.write("&lt;/pre&gt;")
oRS.close
oConn.close
%&gt;
</pre></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1067"><strong>Question 1068. How To Check The Oracle Tns Settings?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>If you have installed an Oracle server or an Oracle client tool on your local system, the TNS is automatically installed with a simple configuration file, tnsnames.ora, to define Oracle connect identifiers.</p>
<p>For example, if you have Oracle XE server installed, you will have the tnsnames.ora located at<br/>
oraclexeapporacleproduct10.2.0serverNETWORKADMIN. It should contain a connect identifier called XE defined as:</p>
<pre>
XE =
(DESCRIPTION =
(ADDRESS =
(PROTOCOL = TCP)(HOST = localhost)
(PORT = 1521)
)
(CONNECT_DATA =
(SERVER = DEDICATED)
(SERVICE_NAME = XE)
)
)
</pre></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1068"><strong>Question 1069. How To Create Tables For Odbc Connection Testing?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>If you want to follow the tutorial exercises in the sections below, you need to create a user account and a table for ODBC connection testing as shown here:</p>
<pre>
SQL&gt; CONNECT system/retneciyf
Connected.
SQL&gt; CREATE USER fyi IDENTIFIED BY retneciyf ACCOUNT UNLOCK;
User created.
SQL&gt; GRANT CREATE SESSION TO fyi;
Grant succeeded.
SQL&gt; GRANT CREATE TABLE TO fyi;
Grant succeeded.
SQL&gt; ALTER USER fyi DEFAULT TABLESPACE USERS;
85
User altered.
SQL&gt; ALTER USER dev QUOTA 4M ON USERS;
User altered.
SQL&gt; connect fyi/retneciyf;
Connected.
SQL&gt; CREATE TABLE dev_faq (id NUMBER);
SQL&gt; INSERT INTO dev_faq VALUES (3);
SQL&gt; INSERT INTO dev_faq VALUES (5);
SQL&gt; INSERT INTO dev_faq VALUES (7);
</pre></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1069"><strong>Question 1070. How Can Windows Applications Connect To Oracle Servers?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>A Windows application can connect to an Oracle server directly, if it knows how to use the Oracle TNS technology. A Windows application can connect to an Oracle server indirectly through Windows ODBC manager, becaused offers ODBC drivers to support the ODBC API. The diagram below shows how MS Access can connect to an Oracle server through the ODBC driver:</p>
<p><img alt="" height="143" src="/userfiles/image/oracle/interview-ques1.jpg" width="400"/></p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1070"><strong>Question 1071. What Is Open Database Communication (odbc)?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>ODBC, Open Database Communication, a standard API (application program interface) developed by Microsoft for Windows applications to communicate with database management systems. Oracle offers ODBC drivers to allow Windows applications to connect Oracle server through ODBC.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1071"><strong>Question 1072. What Are The Original Export And Import Utilities?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Oracle original Export and Import utilities are standalone programs that provide you a simple way for you to transfer data objects between Oracle databases, even if they reside on platforms with different hardware and software configurations. When you run Export against an Oracle database, objects (such as tables) are extracted, followed by their related objects (such as indexes, comments, and grants), if any. The extracted data is written to an export dump file. The Import utility reads the object definitions and table data from the dump file.</p>
<p>An export file is an Oracle binary-format dump file that is typically located on disk or tape. The dump files can be transferred using FTP or physically transported (in the case of tape) to a different site. The files can then be used with the Import utility to transfer data between databases that are on systems not connected through a network. The files can also be used as backups in addition to normal backup procedures.</p>
<p>Export and Import utilities are now being replaced by Data Pump Export and Import utilities in Oracle 10g. But you can still use them.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1072"><strong>Question 1073. How To Import One Table Back From A Dump File?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>If you only want to import one table back to the database, you can use a dump file that was created by full export, schema export or a table export. The following tutorial exercise shows you how to import the "fyi_links" table from a dump file created by a schema export:</p>
<pre>
&gt;cd oraclexeapporacleproduct10.2.0serverBIN
&gt;sqlplus /nolog
SQL&gt; connect HR/fyicenter
SQL&gt; DROP TABLE fyi_links;
Table dropped.
SQL&gt; exit;
&gt;impdp hr/fyicenter TABLES=fyi_links DIRECTORY=hr_dump
DUMPFILE=schema.dmp LOGFILE=tables.log
Master table "HR"."SYS_IMPORT_TABLE_01" loaded/unloaded
Starting "HR"."SYS_IMPORT_TABLE_01": hr/** TABLES=fyi_links
DIRECTORY=hr_dump DUMPFILE=schema.dmp LOGFILE=tables.log
Processing object type SCHEMA_EXPORT/TABLE/TABLE
Processing object type SCHEMA_EXPORT/TABLE/TABLE_DATA
. . imported "HR"."FYI_LINKS" 6.375 KB 4 rows
Processing object type SCHEMA_EXPORT/TABLE/CONSTRAINT/CON...
Processing object type SCHEMA_EXPORT/TABLE/INDEX/STATISTI...
Processing object type SCHEMA_EXPORT/TABLE/STATISTICS/TAB...
Job "HR"."SYS_IMPORT_TABLE_01" successfully completed.
</pre></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1073"><strong>Question 1074. What Happens If The Imported Table Already Exists?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>If the import process tries to import a table that already exists, the Data Pump Import utility will return an error and skip this table. The following exercise shows you a good example:</p>
<pre>
&gt;cd oraclexeapporacleproduct10.2.0serverBIN
&gt;impdp hr/fyicenter TABLES=employees
DIRECTORY=hr_dump DUMPFILE=tables.dmp LOGFILE=tables.log
Master table "HR"."SYS_IMPORT_TABLE_01" loaded/unloaded
Starting "HR"."SYS_IMPORT_TABLE_01": hr/** TABLES=employees
DIRECTORY=hr_dump DUMPFILE=tables.dmp LOGFILE=tables.log
Processing object type TABLE_EXPORT/TABLE/TABLE
ORA-39151: Table "HR"."EMPLOYEES" exists. All dependent
metadata and data will be skipped due to table_exists_action
of skip
Processing object type TABLE_EXPORT/TABLE/TABLE_DATA
Processing object type TABLE_EXPORT/TABLE/INDEX/INDEX
</pre></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1074"><strong>Question 1075. How To Export Several Tables Together?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>If you don't want to export the entire schema and only want to export several tables only, you can use the "expdp" command with the "TABLES" parameter as shown in the following tutorial exercise:</p>
<pre>
&gt;cd oraclexeapporacleproduct10.2.0serverBIN
&gt;expdp hr/fyicenter TABLES=employees,departments
DIRECTORY=hr_dump DUMPFILE=tables.dmp LOGFILE=tables.log
Starting "HR"."SYS_EXPORT_TABLE_01": hr/********
TABLES=employees,departments DIRECTORY=hr_dump
DUMPFILE=tables.dmp
LOGFILE=tables.log
Estimate in progress using BLOCKS method...
Processing object type TABLE_EXPORT/TABLE/TABLE_DATA
Total estimation using BLOCKS method: 128 KB
Processing object type TABLE_EXPORT/TABLE/TABLE
Processing object type TABLE_EXPORT/TABLE/INDEX/INDEX
Processing object type TABLE_EXPORT/TABLE/CONSTRAINT/CON...
Processing object type TABLE_EXPORT/TABLE/INDEX/STATISTI...
Processing object type TABLE_EXPORT/TABLE/COMMENT
Processing object type TABLE_EXPORT/TABLE/CONSTRAINT/REF...
Processing object type TABLE_EXPORT/TABLE/TRIGGER

. . exported "HR"."DEPARTMENTS" 6.632 KB 27 rows
. . exported "HR"."EMPLOYEES" 15.76 KB 107 rows

Dump file set for HR.SYS_EXPORT_TABLE_01 is:
C:ORACLEXEHR_DUMPTABLES.DMP
