</pre></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1075"><strong>Question 1076. What Are Data Pump Export And Import Modes?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Data pump export and import modes are used to determine the type and portions of database to be exported and imported.</p>
<p>Oracle 10g supports 5 export and import modes:</p>
<ul>
<li>Full: Exports and imports a full database. Use the FULL parameter to specify this mode.</li>
<li>Schema: Enables you to export and import all objects that belong to a schema. Use the SCHEMAS parameter to specify this mode. This is the default mode.</li>
<li>Table: Enables you to export and import specific tables and partitions. Use the TABLES parameter to specify this mode.</li>
<li>Tablespace: Enables a privileged user to move a set of tablespaces from one Oracle database to another. Use the TABLESPACES parameter to specify this mode.</li>
<li>Tablespace: Enables a privileged user to move metadata from the tables within a specified set of tablespaces from one Oracle database to another. Use the TRANSPORT_TABLESPACES parameter to specify this mode.</li>
</ul></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1076"><strong>Question 1077. What Is The Data Pump Import Utility?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Oracle Data Pump Import utility is a standalone programs that allows you to import data objects from an Oracle dump file set into Oracle database. Oracle dump file set is written in a proprietary binary format by the Data Pump Export utility. Import can also be used to load a target database directly from a source database with no intervening dump files. This allows export and import operations to run concurrently, minimizing total elapsed time. This is known as a network import.</p>
<p>Data Pump Import enables you to specify whether a job should move a subset of the data and metadata from the dump file set or the source database (in the case of a network import), as determined by the import mode. This is done using data filters and metadata filters, which are implemented through Import commands.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1077"><strong>Question 1078. What Is The Data Pump Export Utility?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Oracle Data Pump Export utility is a standalone programs that allows you to export data objects from Oracle database to operating system files called dump file set, which can be imported back to Oracle database only by Oracle Data Pump Import utility.</p>
<p>The dump file set can be imported on the same system or it can be moved to another system and loaded there. The dump file set is made up of one or more disk files that contain table data, database object metadata, and control information. The files are written in a proprietary, binary format. During an import operation, the Data Pump Import utility uses these files to locate each database object in the dump file set. Because the dump files are written by the server, rather than by the client, the data base administrator (DBA) must create directory objects.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1078"><strong>Question 1079. What Is A Directory Object?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>A directory object is a logical alias for a physical directory path name on the operating system. Directory objects can be created, dropped, and granted access permissions to different users. The following tutorial exercise shows you some good examples:</p>
<pre>
&gt;sqlplus /nolog
SQL&gt; connect SYSTEM/fyicenter
SQL&gt; CREATE DIRECTORY test_dir AS '/oraclexe/test';
Directory created.
SQL&gt; GRANT READ ON DIRECTORY test_dir TO hr;
Grant succeeded.
SQL&gt; GRANT WRITE ON DIRECTORY test_dir TO hr;
Grant succeeded.
SQL&gt; CREATE DIRECTORY temp_dir AS '/oraclexe/temp';
Directory created.
SQL&gt; DROP DIRECTORY temp_dir;
Directory dropped.</pre></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1079"><strong>Question 1080. What Are The Restrictions On External Table Columns?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>When creating external table columns, you need to watch out some restrictions:</p>
<ul>
<li>"PRIMARY KEY" is not allowed.</li>
<li>"NOT NULL" is not allowed.</li>
<li>"DEFAULT value" is not allowed.</li>
</ul></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1080"><strong>Question 1081. How To Load Data Through External Tables?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>If you have data stored in external files, you can load it to database through an external table by the steps below:</p>
<ul>
<li>Create an external table with columns matching data fields in the external file.</li>
<li>Create a regular table with the same columns.</li>
<li>Run an INSERT INTO ... SELECT statement to load data from the external file to the regular table through the external table.</li>
</ul></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1081"><strong>Question 1082. What Is An External Table?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>An external table is a table defined in the database with data stored outside the database. Data of an external table is stored in files on the operating systems. Accessing data of external tables are done through data access drivers. Currently, Oracle supports two data access drivers: ORACLE_LOADER and ORACLE_DATAPUMP.</p>
<p>External tables can be used to load data from external files into database, or unload data from database to external files.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1082"><strong>Question 1083. What Is A Sql*loader Control File?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>A SQL*Loader control file a text that defines how data files should be loaded into the database. It allows you to specify:</p>
<ul>
<li>Where is the input data file.</li>
<li>The format of the input date file.</li>
<li>The target table where the data should be loaded.</li>
<li>How input data fields should be mapped to target table columns.</li>
<li>Select criteria to select input records for loading.</li>
<li>Where to output errors.</li>
</ul></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1083"><strong>Question 1084. What Is Sql*loader?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>SQL*Loader is a database tool that allows to load data from external files into database tables. SQL*Loader is available as part of the free Oracle 10g Expression Edition. It has some interesting features as:</p>
<ul>
<li>Can load data from multiple data files into multiple tables in one load session.</li>
<li>Can specify character set of the data.</li>
<li>Can generate sophisticated error reports.</li>
<li>Can load data directly to Oracle datafiles, bypassing normal record inserting process.</li>
</ul></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1084"><strong>Question 1085. What Is The Simplest Tool To Run Commands On Oracle Servers?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>The simplest tool to connect to an Oracle server and run commands to manage data is SQL*Plus. It is an Oracle database client tool that works as a command-line user interface to the database server. SQL*Plus allows you:</p>
<ul>
<li>Format, perform calculations on, store, and print from query results.</li>
<li>Examine table and object definitions.</li>
<li>Develop and run batch scripts.</li>
<li>Perform database administration.</li>
</ul></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1085"><strong>Question 1086. Why Cursor Variables Are Easier To Use Than Cursors?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Cursor variables are easier to use than cursors because:</p>
<ul>
<li>Cursor variables are easier to define. No need to give a specific query statement.</li>
<li>Cursor variables are easier to open. You can specify the query dynamically at the time of open.</li>
<li>Cursor variables can be passed into procedures or functions.</li>
</ul></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1086"><strong>Question 1087. How To Pass A Cursor Variable To A Procedure?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>A cursor variable can be passed into a procedure like a normal variable. The sample script below gives you a good example:</p>
<pre>
CREATE OR REPLACE PROCEDURE FYI_CENTER AS
sys_cur SYS_REFCURSOR;
PROCEDURE emp_print(cur SYS_REFCURSOR) AS
emp_rec employees%ROWTYPE;
BEGIN
LOOP
FETCH cur INTO emp_rec;
EXIT WHEN cur%NOTFOUND;
DBMS_OUTPUT.PUT_LINE('Name = ' ||
emp_rec.first_name || ' ' || emp_rec.last_name);
END LOOP;
END;
BEGIN
OPEN sys_cur FOR SELECT * FROM employees
WHERE manager_id = 101;
emp_print(sys_cur);
CLOSE sys_cur;
END;
/
Name = Nancy Greenberg
Name = Jennifer Whalen
Name = Susan Mavris
Name = Hermann Baer
Name = Shelley Higgins
</pre></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1087"><strong>Question 1088. How To Loop Through A Cursor Variable?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Once a cursor variable is opened with a query statement, it will have the same attributes as a normal cursor and it can be used in the same way a normal cursor too. The following sample script shows you how to loop through a cursor variable:</p>
<pre>
CREATE OR REPLACE PROCEDURE FYI_CENTER AS
TYPE emp_ref IS REF CURSOR RETURN employees%ROWTYPE;
emp_cur emp_ref;
emp_rec employees%ROWTYPE;
BEGIN
OPEN emp_cur FOR SELECT * FROM employees
WHERE manager_id = 101;
LOOP
FETCH emp_cur INTO emp_rec;
EXIT WHEN emp_cur%NOTFOUND;
DBMS_OUTPUT.PUT_LINE('Name = ' ||
emp_rec.first_name || ' ' || emp_rec.last_name);
END LOOP;
CLOSE emp_cur;
END;
/
Name = Nancy Greenberg
Name = Jennifer Whalen
Name = Susan Mavris
Name = Hermann Baer
Name = Shelley Higgins
</pre></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1088"><strong>Question 1089. How To Open A Cursor Variable?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>A cursor variable must be opened with a specific query statement before you can fetch data fields from its data rows. To open a cursor variable, you can use the OPEN ... FOR statement as shown in the following tutorial exercise:</p>
<pre>
CREATE OR REPLACE PROCEDURE FYI_CENTER AS
TYPE emp_ref IS REF CURSOR RETURN employees%ROWTYPE;
TYPE any_ref IS REF CURSOR;
emp_cur emp_ref;
any_cur any_ref;
sys_cur SYS_REFCURSOR;
BEGIN
OPEN emp_cur FOR SELECT * FROM employees;
OPEN any_cur FOR SELECT * FROM employees;
OPEN sys_cur FOR SELECT * FROM employees;
CLOSE sys_cur;
CLOSE any_cur;
CLOSE emp_cur;
END;
/
</pre></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1089"><strong>Question 1090. How To Define A Cursor Variable?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>To define cursor variable, you must decide which REF CURSOR data type to use. There are 3 ways to select a REF CURSOR data type:</p>
<ul>
<li>Define your own specific REF CURSOR types using the TYPE ... RETURN statement.</li>
<li>Define your own generic REF CURSOR type using the TYPE ... statement.</li>
<li>Use the system defined REF CURSOR type: SYS_REFCURSOR.</li>
</ul>
<p>The follwoing tutorial exercise defines 3 cursor variables in 3 different ways:</p>
<pre>
CREATE OR REPLACE PROCEDURE FYI_CENTER AS
TYPE emp_ref IS REF CURSOR RETURN employees%ROWTYPE;
TYPE any_ref IS REF CURSOR;
emp_cur emp_ref;
any_cur any_ref;
sys_cur SYS_REFCURSOR;
BEGIN
NULL;
END;
/
</pre></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1090"><strong>Question 1091. What Is A Cursor Variable?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>A cursor variable is a variable of a specific REF CURSOR data type, which is a pointer to a data structure resource connects to query statement result, similar to the CURSOR data type.. The advantage of using cursor variables is that cursor variables can be used as variables to pass between procedures and functions.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1091"><strong>Question 1092. Can Multiple Cursors Being Opened At The Same Time?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Yes, multiple cursors can be opened at the same time. See the following example:</p>
<pre>
CREATE OR REPLACE PROCEDURE FYI_CENTER AS
CURSOR emp_cur IS SELECT * FROM employees;
emp_rec employees%ROWTYPE;
CURSOR dpt_cur IS SELECT * FROM departments;
dpt_rec departments%ROWTYPE;
BEGIN
OPEN emp_cur;
OPEN dpt_cur;
FETCH emp_cur INTO emp_rec;
FETCH dpt_cur INTO dpt_rec;
DBMS_OUTPUT.PUT_LINE('Department name = ' ||
dpt_rec.department_name);
DBMS_OUTPUT.PUT_LINE('Employee name = ' ||
emp_rec.first_name || ' ' || emp_rec.last_name);
CLOSE emp_cur;
CLOSE dpt_cur;
END;
/
Department name = Administration
Employee name = Steven King
</pre></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1092"><strong>Question 1093. How To Use An Explicit Cursor Without Open Statements?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>f you want to open a cursor and loop through its data rows in quick way, you can use the FOR ... IN ... LOOP statement in the same way as the implicit cursor. The following tutorial exercise gives you a good example:</p>
<pre>
CREATE OR REPLACE PROCEDURE FYI_CENTER AS
CURSOR emp_cur IS SELECT * FROM employees
WHERE manager_id = 101;
BEGIN
FOR row IN emp_cur LOOP
DBMS_OUTPUT.PUT_LINE('Name = ' ||
row.first_name || ' ' || row.last_name);
END LOOP;
END;
/
Name = Nancy Greenberg
Name = Jennifer Whalen
Name = Susan Mavris
Name = Hermann Baer
Name = Shelley Higgins
</pre></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1093"><strong>Question 1094. How To Use Fetch Statement In A Loop?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>If you have a cursor opened ready to use, you can also use the FETCH statement in a loop to retrieve data from the cursor more efficiently. But you need to remember to use an EXIT statement break the loop when the cursor pointer reaches the end. The script below gives you a good example:</p>
<pre>
CREATE OR REPLACE PROCEDURE FYI_CENTER AS
CURSOR emp_cur IS SELECT * FROM employees
WHERE manager_id = 101;
emp_rec employees%ROWTYPE;
BEGIN
OPEN emp_cur;
LOOP
FETCH emp_cur INTO emp_rec;
EXIT WHEN emp_cur%NOTFOUND;
DBMS_OUTPUT.PUT_LINE('Name = ' ||
emp_rec.first_name || ' ' || emp_rec.last_name);
END LOOP;
CLOSE emp_cur;
END;
/
</pre></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1094"><strong>Question 1095. How To Retrieve Data From An Cursor To A Record?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>If you have a cursor opened ready to use, you can also use the FETCH statement to retrieve data from the cursor into a RECORD variable as shown in the tutorial exercise below:</p>
<pre>
CREATE OR REPLACE PROCEDURE FYI_CENTER AS
CURSOR t_list IS SELECT first_name, last_name
FROM employees;
TYPE name_rec IS RECORD (
f_name VARCHAR2(10),
l_name VARCHAR2(10)
);
n name_rec;
BEGIN
OPEN t_list;
FETCH t_list INTO n;
DBMS_OUTPUT.PUT_LINE('Name = ' || n.f_name || ' '
|| n.l_name);
FETCH t_list INTO n;
DBMS_OUTPUT.PUT_LINE('Name = ' || n.f_name || ' '
75
|| n.l_name);
CLOSE t_list;
END;
/
Name = Ellen Abel
Name = Sundar Ande
</pre></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1095"><strong>Question 1096. How To Open And Close An Explicit Cursor?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>An existing cursor can be opened or closed by the OPEN or CLOSE statement as shown in the following sample script:</p>
<pre>
DECLARE
CURSOR c_list IS SELECT * FROM countries;
CURSOR t_list IS SELECT * FROM employees
WHERE employee_id = 100;
BEGIN
OPEN c_list;
OPEN t_list;
CLOSE c_list;
CLOSE t_list;
END;
/
</pre></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1096"><strong>Question 1097. How To Define An Explicit Cursor?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>An explicit cursor must be defined in the declaration part of a procedure or function with the CURSOR ... IS statement as shown in the following sample script:</p>
<pre>
DECLARE
CURSOR c_list IS SELECT * FROM countries;
CURSOR t_list IS SELECT * FROM employees
WHERE employee_id = 100;
BEGIN
NULL;
END;
/
</pre></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1097"><strong>Question 1098. What Is The Implicit Cursor?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>There is only one implicitly cursor in a session. The implicit cursor is the cursor automatically defined by PL/SQL for you. Whenever a SQL statement is executed, this cursor will be assigned to represent the execution of this statement. This implicit cursor is called SQL. It has many attributes representing some good information about the execution like:</p>
<ul>
<li>SQL%FOUND - True, if the SQL statement has changed any rows.</li>
<li>SQL%NOTFOUND - True, if the SQL statement has not changed any rows.</li>
<li>%ISOPEN - True, if there is a SQL statement being associated to the cursor.</li>
</ul></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1098"><strong>Question 1099. How Many Types Of Cursors Supported In Pl/sql?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>PL/SQL supports two types of cursors:</p>
<ul>
<li>The implicit cursor - A single default cursor that automatically connects to the last DML statement executed.</li>
<li>Explicit cursors - User defined cursors with specific DML statements and execution statuses.</li>
</ul></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1099"><strong>Question 1100. How To Define A Variable To Match A Table Column Data Type?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>If you have a table, and want to define some variables to have exactly the same data types as some columns in that table, you can use table_name.column_name%TYPE as data types to define those variables. The tutorial sample below shows you how to do this:</p>
<pre>
CREATE OR REPLACE PROCEDURE FYI_CENTER AS
my_email employees.email%TYPE;
my_salary employees.salary%TYPE;
BEGIN
SELECT email, salary INTO my_email, my_salary
FROM employees WHERE employee_id = 101;
DBMS_OUTPUT.PUT_LINE('My email = ' || my_email);
DBMS_OUTPUT.PUT_LINE('My salary = ' || my_salary);
73
END;
/
My email = NKOCHHAR
My salary = 17000
</pre></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1100"><strong>Question 1101. How To Update A Table Row With A Record?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>If you have a RECORD variable with data fields matching a table structure, you can update a row in this table with this RECORD variable using the UPDATE ... SET ROW statement as shown in the sample script below:</p>
<pre>
CREATE TABLE emp_temp AS SELECT * FROM employees;
CREATE OR REPLACE PROCEDURE FYI_CENTER AS
manager employees%ROWTYPE;
BEGIN
SELECT * INTO manager FROM employees
WHERE employee_id = 100;
manager.employee_id := 299;
INSERT INTO emp_temp VALUES manager;
manager.first_name := 'FYI';
manager.last_name := 'Center';
UPDATE emp_temp SET ROW = manager WHERE employee_id = 299;
DBMS_OUTPUT.PUT_LINE('# rows updated = ' || SQL%ROWCOUNT);
END;
/
# rows updated = 1
</pre></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1101"><strong>Question 1102. How To Assign A Table Row To A Record Variable?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>If you have a table, and want to assign a data row of that table to a RECORD variable, you need to define this RECORD variable to match the table column structure, then use the SELECT ... INTO statement to assign a data row that RECORD variable. The script below shows you how to do this:</p>
<pre>
CREATE OR REPLACE PROCEDURE FYI_CENTER AS
manager employees%ROWTYPE;
BEGIN
SELECT * INTO manager FROM employees
WHERE employee_id = 100;
DBMS_OUTPUT.PUT_LINE('My manager = ' ||
manager.first_name || ' ' || manager.last_name);
END;
/
My manager = Steven King
</pre></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1102"><strong>Question 1103. How To Define A Record Variable To Store A Table Row?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>If you have a table, and want to define a RECORD variable to store all the data elements of a row from that table, you can use table_name%ROWTYPE to define the RECORD variable as shown in the following sample script:</p>
<pre>
CREATE TABLE student (id NUMBER(5) PRIMARY KEY,
first_name VARCHAR(80) NOT NULL,
last_name VARCHAR(80) NOT NULL);
Table created.
CREATE OR REPLACE PROCEDURE FYI_CENTER AS
best_student student%ROWTYPE;
another_student student%ROWTYPE;
class_name VARCHAR2(80);
BEGIN
class_name := 'FYI Center 2006';
best_student.first_name := 'The';
best_student.last_name := 'Best';
DBMS_OUTPUT.PUT_LINE('Best student ID = '
|| best_student.id);
DBMS_OUTPUT.PUT_LINE('Best student = ' ||
best_student.first_name || ' '
|| best_student.last_name);
END;
/
Best student ID =
Best student = The Best
</pre></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1103"><strong>Question 1104. How To Define A Data Field As Not Null?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>When defining a specific RECORD type, you can define a data field as NOT NULL to make sure variables with this RECORD type to always have values in this field. A field defined as NOT NULL must have a default value. Here is a tutorial script showing you how to define a data field as NOT NULL:</p>
<pre>
CREATE OR REPLACE PROCEDURE HELLO AS
TYPE student IS RECORD (
id NUMBER(5) NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
first_name VARCHAR(80),
last_name VARCHAR(80)
);
best_student student;
another_student student;
class_name VARCHAR2(80);
BEGIN
class_name := 'FYI Center 2006';
best_student.first_name := 'The';
best_student.last_name := 'Best';
DBMS_OUTPUT.PUT_LINE('Best student ID = '
|| best_student.id);
DBMS_OUTPUT.PUT_LINE('Best student = ' ||
best_student.first_name || ' '
|| best_student.last_name);
END;
/
Best student ID = 0
Best student = The Best
</pre></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1104"><strong>Question 1105. How To Retrieve Values From Data Fields In Record Variables?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>If a variable is a RECORD variable with data fields assigned values, you can retrieve those values out of its data fields by using fields names prefixed with variable name as "variable.field_name". Here is a sample script showing you how to retrieve field values from RECORD variables:</p>
<pre>
CREATE OR REPLACE PROCEDURE HELLO AS
TYPE student IS RECORD (
id NUMBER(5),
first_name VARCHAR(80),
last_name VARCHAR(80)
);
best_student student;
another_student student;
class_name VARCHAR2(80);
BEGIN
class_name := 'FYI Center 2006';
best_student.first_name := 'The';
best_student.last_name := 'Best';
DBMS_OUTPUT.PUT_LINE('Best student = ' ||
best_student.first_name || ' '
|| best_student.last_name);
END;
/
Best student = The Best
</pre></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1105"><strong>Question 1106. How To Assign Values To Data Fields In Record Variables?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>If a variable is a RECORD variable, you can assign values to its data fields by using fields names prefixed with variable name as "variable.field_name". Here is a sample script assigning values to data fields of RECORD variables:</p>
<pre>
CREATE OR REPLACE PROCEDURE HELLO AS
TYPE student IS RECORD (
id NUMBER(5),
first_name VARCHAR(80),
last_name VARCHAR(80)
);
best_student student;
another_student student;
class_name VARCHAR2(80);
BEGIN
class_name := 'FYI Center 2006';
best_student.first_name := 'The';
best_student.last_name := 'Best';
END;
/
</pre></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1106"><strong>Question 1107. How To Define A Variable Of A Specific Record Type?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>Once you have your specific RECORD type defined, you can define new variables with this specific RECORD type like any other data type. In the sample script below, several variables are defined with a regular data type and a specific RECORD type:</p>
<pre>
CREATE OR REPLACE PROCEDURE HELLO AS
TYPE student IS RECORD (
id NUMBER(5),
first_name VARCHAR(80),
last_name VARCHAR(80)
);
best_student student;
another_student student;
class_name VARCHAR2(80);
BEGIN
NULL;
END;
/
</pre></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1107"><strong>Question 1108. How To Define A Specific Record Type?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>If you want to define a specific RECORD type, you need to use the TYPE ... IS RECORD statement in the declaration part of any procedure or function. The following example script defines a RECORD type called STUDENT:</p>
<pre>
CREATE OR REPLACE PROCEDURE HELLO AS
TYPE student IS RECORD (
id NUMBER(5),
first_name VARCHAR(80),
last_name VARCHAR(80)
);
BEGIN
NULL;
END;
/
</pre></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1108"><strong>Question 1109. What Is A Record In Pl/sql?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>RECORD is a composite data type in PL/SQL. It can have many fields representing data elements with different data types. Variables of RECORD type can be designed to hold data from database table rows. To use RECORD data type, you need to define a specific RECORD type with each field defined with a name and a data type. Then you can use your specific RECORD type to define your RECORD type variables.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1109"><strong>Question 1110. How To Assign Data Of The Deleted Row To Variables?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>If a DELETE statement is deleting a single row, you can assign column values of the deleted row to variables by using the RETURNING clause, which an extension of DELETE statements for PL/SQL. The tutorial script shows you how to do this:</p>
<pre>
CREATE TABLE emp_temp AS SELECT * FROM employees;
DECLARE
fname VARCHAR2(10);
lname VARCHAR2(10);
BEGIN
DELETE FROM emp_temp WHERE employee_id = 100;
RETURNING first_name, last_name INTO fname, lname;
DBMS_OUTPUT.PUT_LINE('Name deleted = ' || fname || ' '
|| lname);
-- This will not work because multiple rows deleted
-- DELETE FROM emp_temp WHERE employee_id &gt; 100;
-- RETURNING first_name, last_name INTO fname, lname;
END;
/
</pre>
<p>Name deleted = Steven King Similar to SELECT ... INTO, RETURNING ... INTO will not work if multiple rows are deleted.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1110"><strong>Question 1111. How To Retrieve The Count Of Updated Rows?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>After running an UPDATE statement, the database server returns a count of updated rows. You can retrieve this count from a special predefined variable called SQL%ROWCOUT, as shown in the following tutorial:</p>
<pre>
CREATE TABLE emp_temp AS SELECT * FROM employees;
BEGIN
UPDATE emp_temp SET salary = salary * 1.05
WHERE salary &lt; 5000;
DBMS_OUTPUT.PUT_LINE('# of rows updated: ' ||
SQL%ROWCOUNT);
END;
/
# of rows updated: 49
</pre></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1111"><strong>Question 1112. How To Assign Query Results To Variables?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>If you want to assign results from SELECT statements to variables, you can use the INTO clause, which an extension of SELECT statements for PL/SQL. The sample code below shows some good example on INTO clause:</p>
<pre>
DECLARE
total NUMBER;
now DATE;
fname VARCHAR2(10);
lname VARCHAR2(10);
BEGIN
SELECT COUNT(*) INTO total FROM employees;
DBMS_OUTPUT.PUT_LINE('Count = ' || TO_CHAR(total));
SELECT SYSDATE INTO now FROM DUAL;
DBMS_OUTPUT.PUT_LINE('Now = ' || TO_CHAR(now, 'SSSSS'));
SELECT first_name, last_name INTO fname, lname
FROM employees
WHERE employee_id = 100;
DBMS_OUTPUT.PUT_LINE('Name = ' || fname || ' ' || lname);
END;
/
Count = 107
Now = 82375
Name = Steven King
</pre></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1112"><strong>Question 1113. How To Resolve Name Conflicts Between Variables And Columns?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>The best way to resolve name conflicts is to avoid using column names for variables.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1113"><strong>Question 1114. Can Ddl Statements Be Used In Pl/sql?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>No, you can not run any DDL statements is PL/SQL directly. If you try to use the DROP TABLE statement inside PL/SQL, you will get a compilation error as shown below:</p>
<pre>
(Connect to XE with SQL*Plus)
BEGIN
DROP TABLE student; -- compilation error
END;
/
</pre></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1114"><strong>Question 1115. What Happens If Recursive Calls Get Out Of Control?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>What happens if your code has bug on recursive procedure calls, which causes an infinite number nested procedure calls? The answer is so good. Oracle server seems to offer no protection calling stack limit. The script below shows you a badly coded recursive procedure. If you run it on an Oracle 10g XE server on Windows, your server will out of control and keep using virtual memory to satisfy the growing calling stack. You have to reboot your server to control back.</p>
<pre>
SQL&gt; CREATE OR REPLACE PROCEDURE STACK_TEST AS
--Warning: do not run this procedure on your server
PROCEDURE STACK AS
BEGIN
STACK;
END;
BEGIN
STACK;
END;
/
</pre>
<p>SQL&gt; EXECUTE STACK_TEST; (your server keep running with 100% CPU and memory usage)</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1115"><strong>Question 1116. How To Define A Sub Procedure?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>A sub procedure is a named procedure defined and used inside another procedure or function. You need to define a sub procedure in the declaration part of the enclosing procedure or function. Sub procedure definition starts with the PROCEDURE key word. Here is a sample script showing you how to define and use a sub procedure:</p>
<pre>
SQL&gt; CREATE OR REPLACE PROCEDURE HR.DBA_WEEK AS
PROCEDURE DBA_TASK (day VARCHAR2) AS
BEGIN
IF day = 'MONDAY' THEN
DBMS_OUTPUT.PUT_LINE('Checking log files.');
ELSIF day = 'FRIDAY' THEN
DBMS_OUTPUT.PUT_LINE('Rebuild indexes.');
ELSE
DBMS_OUTPUT.PUT_LINE('Reading some papers.');
END IF;
END;
BEGIN
DBA_TASK('MONDAY');
DBA_TASK('TUESDAY');
END;
/
</pre>
<p>SQL&gt; EXECUTE DBA_WEEK; Checking log files. Reading some papers.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1116"><strong>Question 1117. How To Call A Stored Function With Parameters?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>You can define a function that takes parameters, provide values to those parameters when calling the function. Here is a good example of a function with a parameter:</p>
<pre>
SQL&gt; CREATE OR REPLACE FUNCTION GET_DOUBLE(X NUMBER)
RETURN NUMBER AS
BEGIN
RETURN X * 2;
END;
/
</pre>
<p>Function created. SQL&gt; SELECT GET_DOUBLE(36) FROM DUAL;</p>
<p>GET_DOUBLE(36)<br/>
--------------<br/>
72</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1117"><strong>Question 1118. How To Drop A Stored Function?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>If there is an existing stored function and you don't want it any more, you can remove it from the database by using the DROP FUNCTION statement as shown in the following script example:</p>
<pre>
SQL&gt; CREATE OR REPLACE FUNCTION GET_SITE
RETURN VARCHAR2 AS
BEGIN
RETURN 'FYICentere.com';
END;
/
</pre>
<p>Function created. SQL&gt; DROP FUNCTION GET_SITE; Function dropped.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1118"><strong>Question 1119. How To Create A Stored Function?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>A stored function is a function with a specified name and stored into the current database. If you want to create a stored function, you can use the CREATE FUNCTION statement. The example script below creates a stored procedure:</p>
<pre>
SQL&gt; CREATE OR REPLACE FUNCTION GET_SITE
RETURN VARCHAR2 AS
BEGIN
RETURN 'FYICentere.com';
END;
/
</pre>
<p>Function created.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1119"><strong>Question 1120. How To Drop A Stored Procedure?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>If there is an existing stored procedure and you don't want it any more, you can remove it from the database by using the DROP PROCEDURE statement as shown in the following script example:</p>
<pre>
SQL&gt; CREATE PROCEDURE Greeting AS
BEGIN
DBMS_OUTPUT.PUT_LINE('Welcome to FYICenter!');
END;
/
</pre>
<p>Procedure created. SQL&gt; DROP PROCEDURE Greeting; Procedure dropped.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1120"><strong>Question 1121. How To Execute A Stored Procedure?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>If you want to execute a stored procedure, you can use the EXECUTE statement. The example script below shows how to executes a stored procedure:</p>
<pre>
SQL&gt; set serveroutput on;
SQL&gt; CREATE PROCEDURE Greeting AS
BEGIN
DBMS_OUTPUT.PUT_LINE('Welcome to wisdom!');
END;
/
</pre>
<p>Procedure created. SQL&gt; EXECUTE Greeting; Welcome to wisdom!</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1121"><strong>Question 1122. How To Create A Stored Procedure?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>A stored procedure is a procedure with a specified name and stored into the current database. If you want to create a stored procedure, you can use the CREATE PROCEDURE statement. The example script below creates a stored procedure:</p>
<pre>
SQL&gt; CREATE PROCEDURE Greeting AS
BEGIN
DBMS_OUTPUT.PUT_LINE('Welcome to wisdom!');
END;
/
</pre>
<p>Procedure created.</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1122"><strong>Question 1123. What Is A Procedure?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>A procedure is a named program unit. It consists of three parts:</p>
<ul>
<li>Declaration Part - Defining the procedure name, calling parameters, local variables and local procedures. Declaration part is required.</li>
<li>Execution Part - Defining execution logic with executable statements. Execution part is required.</li>
<li>Exception Part - Defining error handling logics. Exception part is optional.</li>
</ul>
<p>Here how a complete procedure should look like:</p>
<pre>
PROCEDURE name (parameter_1, parameter_2) AS
-- Declaration statements
BEGIN
-- Executable statements
EXCEPTION
-- Error handling statements
END;</pre></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1123"><strong>Question 1124. How To Use "for" Statements?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>If you have a block of codes to be executed repeatedly over a range of values, you can use the "FOR ... LOOP" statement. Here is a sample script on FOR statements:</p>
<pre>
DECLARE
total NUMBER := 0;
BEGIN
FOR i IN 1..10 LOOP
total := total + i;
END LOOP;
DBMS_OUTPUT.PUT_LINE('Total: ' || TO_CHAR(total));
END;</pre></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1124"><strong>Question 1125. How To Use "while" Statements?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>If you have a block of codes to be executed repeatedly based a condition, you can use the "WHILE ... LOOP" statement. Here is a sample script on WHILE statements:</p>
<pre>
DECLARE
total NUMBER;
BEGIN
total := 0;
WHILE total &lt; 10 LOOP
total := total+1;
END LOOP;
DBMS_OUTPUT.PUT_LINE('Total counts: ' || TO_CHAR(total));
END;
</pre>
<p>This script should print this: Total counts: 10</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1125"><strong>Question 1126. How To Use "if" Statements On Multiple Conditions?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>If you have multiple blocks of codes to be executed based on different conditions, you can use the "IF ... ELSIF" statement. Here is a sample script on IF statements:</p>
<pre>
DECLARE
day VARCHAR2;
BEGIN
day := 'SUNDAY';
IF day = 'THURSDAY' THEN
DBMS_OUTPUT.PUT_LINE('Checking log files.');
ELSIF day = 'TUESDAY' THEN
DBMS_OUTPUT.PUT_LINE('Helping developers.');
ELSIF day = 'FRIDAY' THEN
DBMS_OUTPUT.PUT_LINE('Rebuild indexes.');
ELSE
DBMS_OUTPUT.PUT_LINE('Reading some papers.');
END IF;
END;
This script should print this:
Reading some papers.
</pre></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1126"><strong>Question 1127. How Many Scalar Data Types Are Supported In Pl/sql?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>PL/SQL supports many scalar data types divided into 4 groups:</p>
<p>Numeric Types: BINARY_DOUBLE, BINARY_FLOAT, BINARY_INTEGER, DEC, DECIMAL, DOUBLE PRECISION, FLOAT, INT, INTEGER, NATURAL, NATURALN, NUMBER, NUMERIC, PLS_INTEGER, POSITIVE, POSITIVEN,REAL, SIGNTYPE, SMALLINT.</p>
<ul>
<li>Character Types: CHAR, CHARACTER, LONG, LONG RAW, NCHAR, NVARCHAR2, RAW, ROWID, STRING,UROWID, VARCHAR, VARCHAR2.</li>
<li>Boolean Types: BOOLEAN.</li>
<li>Date Types: DATE, TIMESTAMP, TIMESTAMP WITH TIMEZONE, TIMESTAMP WITH LOCAL TIMEZONE,INTERVAL YEAR TO MONTH, INTERVAL DAY TO SECOND.</li>
</ul></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1127"><strong>Question 1128. What Are The Logical Operations?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>PL/SQL supports 3 logical operations as shown in the following sample script:</p>
<pre>
PROCEDURE proc_comparison AS
x BOOLEAN := TRUE;
y BOOLEAN := FALSE;
res BOOLEAN;
BEGIN
res = x AND y;
res = x OR y;
res = NOT x;
-- more statements
END;
</pre></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1128"><strong>Question 1129. How Many Categories Of Data Types?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>PL/SQL data types are grouped into 4 categories:</p>
<ul>
<li>Scalar Data Types: A scalar data type holds a single value.</li>
<li>Composite Data Types: A composite data type has internal components, such as the elements of an array.</li>
<li>LOB Data Types: A LOB data type holds a lob locator that specify the location of a large object.</li>
<li>Reference Data Types: A reference data type holds a pointer that points to another data object.</li>
</ul></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1129"><strong>Question 1130. What Are The Numeric Comparison Operations?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>PL/SQL supports 6 basic numeric comparison operations as shown in the following sample script:</p>
<pre>
PROCEDURE proc_comparison AS
res BOOLEAN;
BEGIN
res := 1 = 2;
res := 1 &lt; 2;
res := 1 &gt; 2;
res := 1 &lt;= 2;
res := 1 &gt;= 2;
res := 1 &lt;&gt; 2;
-- more statements
END;
</pre></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1130"><strong>Question 1131. What Are The Arithmetic Operations?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>There are 4 basic arithmetic operations on numeric values as shown in the following sample script:</p>
<pre>
PROCEDURE proc_arithmetic AS
addition NUMBER;
subtraction NUMBER;
multiplication NUMBER;
division NUMBER;
BEGIN
addition := 7 + 8;
subtraction := addition - 7;
multiplication := subtraction * 5;
division := multiplication / 8;
-- division should contain 5 now
END;
</pre></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1131"><strong>Question 1132. How To Assign Values To Variables?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>You can use assignment statements to assign values to variables. An assignment statement contains an assignment operator ":=", which takes the value specified on the right to the variable on left. The script below show you some examples of assignment statements:</p>
<pre>
PROCEDURE proc_var_2 AS
is_done BOOLEAN;
counter NUMBER := 0;
message VARCHAR2(80);
BEGIN
is_done := FASLE;
counter := counter + 1;
message := 'Hello world!';
END;
</pre></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1132"><strong>Question 1133. How To Initialize Variables With Default Values?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>There are two ways to assign default values to variables at the time of declaration:</p>
<ul>
<li>Using key word DEFAULT - Appending "DEFAULT value" to the end of declaration statements.</li>
<li>Using assignment operator - Appending ":= value" to the end of declaration statements.</li>
</ul>
<p>The script below show you some examples of declaration statements with default values:</p>
<pre>
PROCEDURE proc_var_1 AS
domain VARCHAR2(80) := 'fyicenter.com';
price REAL DEFAULT 999999.99;
is_for_sale CHAR := 'N';
BEGIN
-- Executable statements
END;
</pre></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1133"><strong>Question 1134. How To Declare A Local Variable?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>A local variable can be defined in the declaration part with a declaration statement, which is a variable name followed a data type identifier. Below are some examples of declaration statements:</p>
<pre>
PROCEDURE proc_var_1 AS
domain VARCHAR2(80);
price REAL;
is_for_sale CHAR;
BEGIN
-- Executable statements
END;
</pre></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1134"><strong>Question 1135. What Is An Anonymous Block?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>An anonymous block is a PL/SQL code block with no name. It consists of three parts:</p>
<ul>
<li><em><strong>Declaration Part</strong></em> - Defining local variables and local procedures. Declaration part is optional.</li>
<li><em><strong>Execution Part</strong></em> - Defining execution logic with executable statements. Execution part is required.</li>
<li><em><strong>Exception Part</strong></em> - Defining error handling logics. Exception part is optional.</li>
</ul>
<p>Here how a complete anonymous block should look like:</p>
<p>DECLARE  // Declaration statements<br/>
BEGIN  // Executable statements<br/>
EXCEPTION  // Error handling statements<br/>
END;</p></p>
</li><br><br><li class="quesans mb-20">
<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1135"><strong>Question 1136. What Do You Think About Oracle Sql Developer?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>To conclude this introductory FAQ collection, you should think about Oracle SQL Developer in comparison with other client tools like SQL*Plus and OracleWeb interface. SQL Developer is definitely better than the other tools, more functionality, and much easier to use. The script debugging mode is very useful.</p></p>

<ul>
<li>Database parameters</li>
<li>Storage information</li>
<li>Session information</li>
<li>Cursors</li>
<li>Data objects</li>
<li>User accounts</li>
<li>Security informaiton</li>
</ul></p>

Your copy of Oracle SQL Developer is running now. There will nothing under the Connections icon, because you haven't defined any connections yet.</p>

<p><a class="accordion-trigger ques" id="ques1139"><strong>Question 1140. How To Create An Oracle Database?</strong></a></p>
<p><span class="ans"><strong>Answer :</strong></span><p>There are two ways to create a new database:</p>
<ul>
<li>Use the Database Configuration Assistant (DBCA) to create a database interactively.</li>
<li>Use the CREATE DATABASE statement to create a database manually.</li>
</ul></p>
